Spousal Shares in Inheritance: Husband and Wife
States Quranic shares for husband and wife with and without children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic shares for husband and wife, apply the condition of having children, and identify the exception of 'awl and the case of multiple spouses.

Core Idea
Spousal shares are fixed by Quran: husband half or fourth, wife fourth or eighth, depending on the presence of children.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the fixed shares for husband and wife derived directly from Surah an-Nisa verse 12. The author shows how the presence of a child (including a grandchild) reduces the share, and also addresses exceptional cases: when the total shares exceed the estate ('awl) and when multiple husbands claim the same deceased wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories for each spouse
For the husband: half if no child, quarter if child. For the wife: quarter if no child, eighth if child. Note that 'child' includes son's child (grandson) descending.
The condition is the existence of any descendant child, including grandchildren.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Surah an-Nisa 4:12 provides the shares: 'lakum nisfu...' for husband, 'lahunna rubu'...' for wife. The particle 'in' (if) creates the conditional distinction.
The imperative form indicates fixed shares (fard).
3
Interpret the key term 'walad'
In Hanafi fiqh, 'walad' includes grandchildren (son's child) based on consensus. This affects share reduction even if the descendents are not immediate children.
This is a Hanafi-specific interpretation; some schools may limit 'walad' to immediate children.
4
Note the exceptions
The share can change only in one case: 'awl (when the total of shares exceeds the estate). In 'awl, all shares are proportionally reduced. Additionally, if multiple men prove marriage to the same deceased woman, they share the husband's share equally per Muhammad's ruling.
The rule for multiple husbands is a special case from Imam Muhammad recorded in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللزوج النصف ومع الولد وولد الابن وإن سفل الربع) لقوله تعالى ولكم نصف ما ترك أزواجكم إن لم يكن لهن ولد فإن كان لهن ولد فلكم الربع مما تركن [النساء : ١٢] فيستحق كل زوج إما النصف وإما الربع مما تركت المرأة لأنها مقابلة الجمع بالجمع يقتضي مقابلة الفرد بالفرد كقولهم ركب القوم دوابهم ولبسوا ثيابهم، ولفظ الولد يتناول ولد الابن فيكون مثله بالنصف أو بالإجماع على ما بينا من قبل، سواء كان من الزوج الوارث الولد أو ولد الولد أو من زوج غيره أو لا يعرف له أب كولد اللعان وغيره فيكون له الربع . معه فصار للزوج حالتان : النصف الربع. وفي شرح الطحاوي : فرض الزوج ما ذكرنا ولا يزاد على النصف ولا ينقص من الربع إلا في حالة العول. قال محمد: والواحد من الأزواج والجماعة في استحقاقهم سهم الأزواج على السواء حتى إن جماعة لو ادعوا نكاح امرأة ولم تكن المرأة في بيت واحد منهم ولا دخل بها واحد منهم لا يعرف أنهم أول فأقام كل واحد منهم البينة على نكاحها فماتت المراة قبل أن يقضي القاضي بميراث غير زوج واحد ويكون بينهم بالسوية ذكر محمد المرأة في كتاب النكاح ووضعها في الرجلين. قال رحمه الله : (وللزوجة الربع) أي للزوجة نصف ما للزوج فيكون لها الربع حيث لا ولد ومع الولد أو ولد الابن وإن سفل الثمن لقوله تعالى ولهن الربع مما تركتم إن لم يكن لكم ولد فإن كان لكم ولد فلهن الثمن مما تركتم [النساء : ۱۲] وإذا كثرن وقعت المزاحمة بينهن فيصرف عليهم جميعاً على السواء لعدم الأولوية فصار للزوجات حالتان: الربع بلا ولد والثمن مع الولد. وفي شرح الطحاوي لا يزدن على الربع ولا ينقص عن الثمن إلا في حالة العول هكذا حكم بيان أصحاب الفرائض من النساء الزوجات.
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And for the husband is half, and with child and child of the son even if descending, the fourth.' by the saying of Allah Most High: 'And for you is half of what your wives leave if they have no child; but if they have a child, then for you is a fourth of what they leave' [an-Nisa 4:12]. So each husband deserves either half or a fourth of what the woman left, because the wording 'for you' (lakum plural) addressing the collectivity implies individual addressing, like their saying: 'the people rode their mounts and wore their clothes.' The word 'child' includes the child of the son, so it is like him by half or by consensus as we explained before, whether the child from the inheriting husband or child or child's child, or from another husband, or one whose father is unknown like the child of li'an and others, then he gets the fourth with him. So for the husband there are two states: half and fourth. In Sharh al-Tahawi: The prescribed share of the husband is what we mentioned; he is not increased beyond half nor decreased below a fourth except in the case of 'awl. Muhammad said: The one husband and the group are equal in entitlement to the share of husbands, such that if a group claims marriage to a woman, and the woman is not in the house of any one of them and none of them has consummated with her, and it is not known who is first, and each one establishes evidence of marriage, and the woman dies before the judge decides, then each gets a share of inheritance and it is divided among them equally. This was mentioned by Muhammad in the book of Nikah and placed it in the chapter on two men. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And for the wife is the fourth.' i.e., the wife gets half of what the husband has, so she gets the fourth where there is no child, and with child or child of the son even if descending, the eighth, by the saying of Allah Most High: 'And for them is a fourth of what you leave if you have no child; but if you have a child, then for them is an eighth of what you leave' [an-Nisa 4:12]. And when they are many, competition occurs among them, and it is distributed among them all equally due to lack of priority. So for wives there are two states: fourth without child and eighth with child. In Sharh al-Tahawi: They are not increased beyond a fourth nor decreased below an eighth except in the case of 'awl. This is the ruling explained by the masters of inheritance regarding women wives.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expounds the spousal shares as per the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins with the husband's share: half if no child, a fourth if there is a child, including son's child descending. The Quranic proof is cited (an-Nisa 4:12). The author explains that the plural 'azwaj' implies each husband individually. The term 'walad' includes son's child by consensus. The husband's share is fixed except in 'awl (when the total exceeds the fund). A unique case from Muhammad: if multiple men claim marriage to a woman each with evidence, and none is known to be first, they share the husband's share equally. Then the wife's share: a fourth without child, an eighth with child. Quranic proof (an-Nisa 4:12). Multiple wives share the fraction equally. Again, no increase or decrease except in 'awl. This is straightforward faraid.

Key Terms
زوج (zawj): Husband, entitled to 1/2 or 1/4 of wife's estate.
زوجة (zawjah): Wife, entitled to 1/4 or 1/8 of husband's estate.
ولد الابن (walad al-ibn): Son's child (grandson) is included in 'child' for purposes of reducing spousal share.
عول ('awl): Proportional reduction of all shares when the sum of fractions exceeds the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman dies leaving a husband, two sons, and a daughter. What is the husband's share?
A) 1/2
B) 1/4
C) 1/8
D) 0 (excluded by children)

Key Takeaway
Spousal shares are fixed Quranic fard: husband receives half or fourth, wife receives fourth or eighth, depending on the presence of a child (including grandchildren).

The Paternal Grandmother is Blocked by the Father
Refutes the view of some tabi'un that the paternal grandmother inherits with the father.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the paternal grandmother's inheritance in the presence of the father, explain the proofs (hadith and qiyas) used by both sides, and apply the concept of hajb hirman.

Core Idea
The paternal grandmother is blocked by the father because she inherits through him, like a daughter of a son.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a dispute among early scholars: does the paternal grandmother (Umm al-Ab) inherit one-sixth when the father is alive? Some tabi'un said yes, citing a hadith and analogy. The Hanafi school firmly says no—she is blocked (hajb hirman) by the father. This lesson dissects the arguments and clarifies the Hanafi position based on both textual evidence and qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
What is the exact issue? Determine whether the paternal grandmother inherits when the father is present. Note the two opposing positions.
The dispute is about Umm al-Ab specifically, not the maternal grandmother.
2
Examine the opposing view and its proofs
State the tabi'un view: she gets 1/6 with the father. List their dalils: (1) a hadith where the Prophet gave inheritance to a grandmother while her son was alive; (2) analogy to the maternal grandmother, who is not blocked by the father; (3) she inherits by fard, so 'asaba should not block her.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim; it is referenced as a specific incident.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: hadith interpretation
The Hanafi response argues that the hadith is a specific case (hikayat hal) and the 'son' was actually a paternal uncle, not a father. Therefore, it does not prove inheritance with a father.
This is a critique of the dalil naqli.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response: qiyas and analogy
The Hanafi school uses qiyas: paternal grandmother is like a daughter of a son (bint al-ibn) who is blocked by the son. Both are connected through an intermediate. Also, she inherits the father's share (1/6), not the mother's, so the maternal grandmother analogy fails.
This is the core qiyas argument. The illa is 'connection through an intermediate' (intisaab bi'l-waasita).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the states of the grandmother
The passage concludes that the grandmother has only two states: she either gets 1/6 (no father) or is completely blocked (father present). This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جعلوا لها السدس مع الأب وبه أخذ طائفة من أهل العلم من التابعين لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ورث جدة وابنها حي ولأنها ترث ميراث الأم فلا يحجبها الأب كما لا يحجب الأم وكما لا يحجب الجد، ولأنها ترث بطريق الفرض فلا تكون العصوبة حاجبة لها كما لا يحجبها عم الميت الذي هو ابنها. قلنا إن أم الأب تدلي بالأب فلا ترث مع وجوده كبنت الابن مع الابن ولا حجة لهم في الحديث لأنه حكاية حال فيحمل أن ذلك الأب كان عماً للميت لا أباً ولا نسلم أنها ترث ميراث الأم بل ميراث الأب لأن له السدس فرضاً فترث ذلك عند عدمه، ولئن كان ميراث الأم لا يلزم منه عدم الحجب بغيره ره ألا تری بنات الابن يرثن ومع هذا يحجبن بالأبوين، وكذا الجد يحجب أبويه لما ذكرنا إلا أم الأب فإنها لا يحجبها وإن علت لأن إرثها ليس من قبله وكذا كل جدة لا تحجب الجدة التي ليست من قبلها فصارت الجدة لها حالتان السدس والسقوط .
They gave her one-sixth with the father, and a group of scholars among the followers (tabi'un) adopted this, based on the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave inheritance to a grandmother while her son was alive, and because she inherits the inheritance of a mother, so the father does not block her just as he does not block the mother, and just as the grandfather does not block her, and because she inherits by way of a prescribed share, so the agnatic relationship does not block her just as the paternal uncle of the deceased who is her son does not block her. We say: the father's mother is connected through the father, so she does not inherit in his presence, like the daughter of a son in the presence of a son. And they have no proof in the hadith because it is a report of a specific state, so it is interpreted that that father was a paternal uncle of the deceased, not a father. And we do not concede that she inherits the inheritance of a mother; rather, she inherits the inheritance of a father because he has one-sixth as a prescribed share, so she inherits that in his absence. And even if it were the inheritance of a mother, it would not necessitate the absence of blocking by others. Do you not see that the daughters of a son inherit, yet they are blocked by both parents? Similarly, the grandfather blocks his parents as we mentioned, except the father's mother, for he does not block her even if he is high, because her inheritance is not from his side. Similarly, every grandmother does not block a grandmother who is not from her side. So the grandmother has two states: one-sixth and complete blockage.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the inheritance of the paternal grandmother (Umm al-Ab). Some early scholars (a group of tabi'un) held that she inherits one-sixth even when the father is present, citing a hadith and analogy to the maternal grandmother. The Hanafi response refutes this: the paternal grandmother is connected through the father, so she is blocked by him, just as a daughter of a son is blocked by a son. The hadith is a specific incident, not a general rule, and the man in the story was a paternal uncle, not a father. Moreover, she does not inherit the mother's share but the father's share. The passage concludes that the paternal grandmother has only two states: one-sixth in the absence of the father, or total blockage in his presence. The reasoning uses both textual evidence (the hadith) and analogical reasoning (qiyas).

Key Terms
جدة (jaddah): In this passage, jaddah refers to the paternal grandmother (Umm al-Ab), whose inheritance status is disputed.
حجب (hajb): The legal prevention of an heir from inheriting due to the presence of a closer heir.
تعصيب (ta'sib): Making someone an 'asaba (agnatic heir) who takes the residue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what is the ruling regarding the paternal grandmother (Umm al-Ab) when the father is alive?
A) She inherits one-sixth.
B) She is completely blocked (hajb hirman) and does not inherit.
C) She inherits one-third.
D) She inherits half.

Key Takeaway
The paternal grandmother inherits only when the father is absent; if the father is alive, she is completely blocked.

Husband's Share in Inheritance
States husband's fixed shares with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the husband's share in inheritance and apply the rule when a son's grandchild is present.

Core Idea
Husband receives half of wife's estate if no child, quarter if child (including son's grandchild).

In this lesson, we examine the fixed share of a husband when his wife dies. The ruling is directly from the Quran and specifies two scenarios: no child vs. child. Understanding what counts as a 'child' (walad) in Hanafi faraid is essential, as it includes grandchildren through a son. We also touch on exceptions like 'awl and rulings for multiple husbands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
State the husband's share: half if the wife left no child, quarter if she left a child. Note that 'child' includes a son's descendant (including grandchild) per Hanafi definition.
The passage clarifies that the share is either half or quarter, no other rates.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The ruling is from An-Nisa 4:12. Read the verse: 'And for you is half of what your wives leave if they have no child; but if they have a child, then for you is one quarter.'
The verse is definitive (qat'i) in transmission and meaning.
3
Understand the definition of walad
Walad in inheritance includes the son's child (grandson/granddaughter) but not a daughter's child. This is based on consensus and the principle that walad refers to descendants through males.
This affects whether a surviving grandchild triggers the quarter share.
4
Note the exception of 'awl
The shares are fixed except in 'awl (proportional reduction when estate is insufficient). In 'awl, the husband's share may be reduced from its normal fraction.
'Awl is a recognized mechanism in Hanafi faraid.
5
Apply to a scenario with multiple claimants
If multiple men claim to be the husband of a deceased woman and all provide proof, they share the husband's portion equally (as per Imam Muhammad). This is an edge case.
This rule is from the Book of Marriage and applies when paternity is unclear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللزوج النصف ومع الولد وولد الابن وإن سفل الربع) لقوله تعالى ولكم نصف ما ترك أزواجكم إن لم يكن لهن ولد فإن كان لهن ولد فلكم الربع مما تركن [النساء : ١٢] فيستحق كل زوج إما النصف وإما الربع مما تركت المرأة لأنها مقابلة الجمع بالجمع يقتضي مقابلة الفرد بالفرد كقولهم ركب القوم دوابهم ولبسوا ثيابهم، ولفظ الولد يتناول ولد الابن فيكون مثله بالنصف أو بالإجماع على ما بينا من قبل، سواء كان من الزوج الوارث الولد أو ولد الولد أو من زوج غيره أو لا يعرف له أب كولد اللعان وغيره فيكون له الربع . معه فصار للزوج حالتان : النصف الربع. وفي شرح الطحاوي : فرض الزوج ما ذكرنا ولا يزاد على النصف ولا ينقص من الربع إلا في حالة العول. قال محمد: والواحد من الأزواج والجماعة في استحقاقهم سهم الأزواج على السواء حتى إن جماعة لو ادعوا نكاح امرأة ولم تكن المرأة في بيت واحد منهم ولا دخل بها واحد منهم لا يعرف أنهم أول فأقام كل واحد منهم البينة على نكاحها فماتت المراة قبل أن يقضي القاضي بميراث غير زوج واحد ويكون بينهم بالسوية ذكر محمد المرأة في كتاب النكاح ووضعها في الرجلين.
He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And for the husband is half, and with a child or a child of a son, even if low, one quarter) due to His statement, the Exalted: 'And for you is half of what your wives leave if they have no child; but if they have a child, then for you is one quarter of what they leave' [An-Nisa 4:12]. So each husband deserves either half or one quarter of what the woman left, because the pairing of plural with plural necessitates pairing of singular with singular, as in the saying: the people rode their mounts and wore their clothes. And the word child (walad) includes the child of a son, so it is like him in half, or by consensus as we explained before, whether the child or child of a son is from the husband who is the heir or from another husband, or is not known to have a father like the child of li'an and others, so he has one quarter with him. So the husband has two states: half and one quarter. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: The prescribed share of the husband is as we mentioned; he is not increased beyond half nor decreased from one quarter except in the case of 'awl. Muhammad said: The one husband and the group of husbands in their entitlement to the share of husbands are equal, to the extent that if a group of men claim marriage to a woman, and the woman was not in the house of any one of them, nor did any one of them have intercourse with her, and they are not known to be first, and each one of them establishes evidence of his marriage to her, then the woman dies before the judge rules on inheritance, then it is not given to any one husband, but is divided equally among them. Muhammad mentioned the woman in the Book of Marriage and placed it in the case of two men.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage from the commentary explains the husband's share in inheritance as stated in the matn. The husband receives half of the deceased wife's estate if she left no children (including children of a son), and one quarter if she left a child. The proof is from Quran 4:12. The commentary clarifies that 'walad' includes a son's child, so a grandchild (through a son) also triggers the quarter share. This applies whether the child is from the inheriting husband or from a previous husband, and even includes a child of li'an. The commentary also notes from Sharh al-Tahawi that these shares are fixed except in 'awl (proportional reduction of shares when estate is insufficient). Imam Muhammad adds that if multiple men claim to be the husband of a woman and she dies before the dispute is resolved, they all share the husband's portion equally if each provides proof of marriage.

Key Terms
ولد (walad): In this context, walad includes both a child and a grandchild through a son (child of a son).
عول ('awl): A proportional reduction of all shares when the estate is insufficient to pay all prescribed shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife dies leaving a husband and a son, what share does the husband receive?
A) One-half
B) One-quarter
C) One-eighth
D) One-sixth

Key Takeaway
The husband's share is fixed by the Quran: half without child, quarter with child (including son's grandchildren).

Wife's Share in Inheritance
States the wife's share: quarter without child, eighth with child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wife's prescribed share in two scenarios and apply the rule to multiple wives.

Core Idea
The wife's share is quarter without child, eighth with child — fixed by explicit Quranic text.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq specifies the wife's inheritance share. The ruling is straightforward but has two conditions depending on the presence of descendants. We will parse the text, identify the Quranic proof, and see how multiple wives share the portion equally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text states two situations: no child (quarter) and with child (eighth). 'Child' includes a son's child even if low in lineage.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
The author cites Quran 4:12 directly. Find the exact wording and note that it explicitly mentions both cases.
The hadith is not needed; this is a Quranic ruling.
3
Apply to multiple wives
If there are multiple wives, the prescribed portion (quarter or eighth) is divided equally among them. No priority among wives.
4
Note the exception of 'awl
The share is fixed except in 'awl (proportional reduction when shares exceed the estate). This is noted from Sharh al-Tahawi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللزوجة الربع) أي للزوجة نصف ما للزوج فيكون لها الربع حيث لا ولد ومع الولد أو ولد الابن وإن سفل الثمن لقوله تعالى ولهن الربع مما تركتم إن لم يكن لكم ولد فإن كان لكم ولد فلهن الثمن مما تركتم [النساء : ۱۲] وإذا كثرن وقعت المزاحمة بينهن فيصرف عليهم جميعاً على السواء لعدم الأولوية فصار للزوجات حالتان: الربع بلا ولد والثمن مع الولد. وفي شرح الطحاوي لا يزدن على الربع ولا ينقص عن الثمن إلا في حالة العول هكذا حكم بيان أصحاب الفرائض من النساء الزوجات.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And for the wife is one quarter) i.e., for the wife half of what the husband gets, so she gets one quarter when there is no child; and with a child or a child of a son, even if low, one eighth, due to His statement: 'And for you is one quarter of what you leave if you have no child; but if you have a child, then for them is one eighth of what you leave' [An-Nisa 4:12]. And when there are multiple wives, competition occurs among them, so the share is distributed among them all equally due to the absence of any priority. So the wives have two states: one quarter without a child, and one eighth with a child. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: They are not increased beyond one quarter nor decreased from one eighth except in the case of 'awl. Thus is the ruling regarding female spouses according to the masters of fara'id.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage states the wife's share. She receives one quarter of the husband's estate if he died without children (including grandchildren through a son), and one eighth if there is a child. The proof is from the same verse as the husband's share (An-Nisa 4:12). If there are multiple wives, they share the prescribed portion equally. The commentary notes from Sharh al-Tahawi that these shares are fixed except in 'awl, where shares are proportionally reduced.

Key Terms
زوجة (zawjah): Wife of the deceased; multiple wives share the prescribed portion equally.
ربع (rub'): One quarter.
ثمن (thumn): One eighth.
ولد (walad): Child (includes son's child even if low in lineage).
عول ('awl): Proportional reduction of all shares when the sum of fractions exceeds the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man dies leaving a widow and a son. What is the widow's share?
A) One-half
B) One-quarter
C) One-eighth
D) One-sixth

Key Takeaway
The wife's share is fixed by Quran as 1/4 without a child and 1/8 with a child, divided equally among multiple wives.

One Daughter's Share: Half
States a faraid ruling with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the share of a single daughter in Hanafi inheritance law and identify the Quranic proof for it.

Core Idea
A single daughter inherits half of the estate — this is a fixed Quranic share.

This lesson presents a foundational ruling in the science of fara'id (inheritance): the share of a single daughter. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq concisely states the rule and cites its direct Quranic evidence. Understanding this share is essential before learning how multiple daughters or the co-existence of sons modify it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heir
The heir in this ruling is the daughter (bint) of the deceased. She is a Quranic heir (sahibat fard).
2
State her share
The text clearly states 'half' (al-nisf). This is the fixed portion for a single daughter when she is the only daughter and there is no son.
3
Cite the Quranic proof
The proof is from Surah An-Nisa, verse 11: 'And if she is one, for her is one half.' This is a direct and explicit textual evidence (nass qat'i).
4
Recognize the category
This share is a fard (fixed obligatory portion) in Hanafi terminology. It is not subject to reduction except in specific circumstances (e.g., 'awl).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللبنت النصف) لقوله تعالى وإن كانت واحدة فلها النصف [النساء: ١١]
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And for the daughter is one half) due to His statement: 'And if she is one, for her is one half' [An-Nisa 4:11].
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This brief passage states the share of a single daughter: she receives half of the estate. The proof is directly from the Quran, Surah An-Nisa, verse 11. This is a foundational ruling in fara'id.

Key Terms
بنت (bint): Daughter of the deceased; she is a Quranic heir (sahibat fard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a deceased leaves only one daughter and no other heirs, what is her share?
A) One-third
B) One-half
C) Two-thirds
D) Entire estate

Key Takeaway
A single daughter inherits half of the estate as a fixed Quranic share.

Two or More Daughters: Two-Thirds and the Refutation of Ibn Abbas
Establishes two-thirds for two or more daughters, refuting Ibn Abbas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for two or more daughters in inheritance, explain the evidence from Quran and Sunnah, and evaluate the counterargument of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Two or more daughters inherit two-thirds, not half—the Quranic plural includes the dual, confirmed by the Sunnah.

This lesson resolves a key dispute in inheritance law: what share do two daughters receive when there is no son? The Hanafi school, following the majority of Companions, holds that they take two-thirds collectively. The dissenting opinion of Ibn Abbas, who argued for half based on the Quranic phrase 'above two', is analyzed and refuted using the Prophet's explicit Sunnah and the principle that the plural can include the dual in Arabic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Positions
State the Hanafi position (two-thirds for two or more daughters) and the opposing view of Ibn Abbas (half for two daughters).
2
Analyze the Quranic Proof
Examine the verse 'if they are women above two, then for them is two-thirds' (An-Nisa 4:11). Understand how the Hanafis interpret the plural 'nisa' to include the dual (two daughters) based on Arabic usul and the context of inheritance.
The Hanafi principle: the plural can refer to the dual unless a separate indicator restricts it.
3
Examine the Sunnah Evidence
Review the hadith of Sa'd's daughters where the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave two daughters two-thirds, one-eighth to the mother, and the remainder to the uncle. This is a direct textual proof for two daughters.
The hadith is narrated by Jabir and is authentic.
4
Address the Counterargument
Evaluate Ibn Abbas's argument: when a son is present, two daughters get half (since the son takes half and his share is double that of a daughter). The Hanafi response: that distribution is due to the son's presence (ta'sib), not their independent share.
The single daughter gets one-third with a son, not half, further supporting the two-thirds independent share.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: following the majority view, two daughters get two-thirds, leaving one-third for other heirs. Following Ibn Abbas, they get half, increasing other heirs' shares.
The Hanafi ruling protects the daughters' prescribed share and is relied upon in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والأكثر الثلثان) وهو قول عامة الصحابة رضي الله عنهم وبه أخذ علماء الأمصار. وعن ابن عباس أنه جعل حكم الثنتين منهن حكم الواحدة فجعل لهما النصف لقوله تعالى فإن كن نساء فوق اثنتين فلهن ثلث ما ترك ﴾ [ النساء : ١١] علق استحقاق الثلثين بكونهن نساء وهو جمع، وصرح بقوله «فوق اثنتين فلهن ثلثا ما ترك» والمعلق بشرط لا يثبت بدونه ولأن الله تعالى جعل للبنتين النصف مع الابن وهو يستحق النصف وحظ الذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين فعلم بذلك أن حظ البنتين النصف عند الإنفراد وللجمهور ما روي عن جابر أنه قال : جاءت امرأة سعد بن الربيع إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بابنتيها من سعد فقالت : يا رسول الله هاتان ابنتا سعد بن الربيع قتل أبوهما معك في أحد شهيداً وإن عمهما أخذ مالهما فلم يدع لهما مالاً ولا ينكحان إلا بمال فقال : يقضي الله في ذلك فنزلت آية الميراث، فأرسل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى عمهما فقال : أعط بنتي سعد الثلثين وأمهما الثمن وما بقي فهو لك. وما تلي لا ينافي استحقاق البنتين الثلثين لأن تخصيص الشيء بالذكر لا ينفي الحكم عما عداه على ما عرف في موضعه فعرفنا حكم الجمع بالكتاب وحكم المثنى بالسنة، ولأن الجمع قد يراد به التثنية لا سيما في الميراث على ما بينا من قبل فيكون المثنى مراداً بالآية وهو الظاهر ألا ترى أن الله تعالى لما بين حكم الجمع والمثنى جعل حكمهما كحكم الجمع في الأخوات لأب وأم أو لأب أو لأم في استحقاق الثلثين أو الثلث. وقوله أن البنتين يستحقان النصف مع «الابن قلنا استحقاقهما ذلك عند الاجتماع لا يدل على استحقاقها إياه عند الانفراد والواحدة تأخذ الثلث مع الابن عند الانفراد.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And for more than one is two-thirds). This is the saying of the generality of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and the scholars of the regions adopted it. It is narrated from Ibn Abbas that he made the ruling for two daughters like the ruling for one, so he gave them half, due to His statement: 'But if they are women above two, then for them is two-thirds of what he left' [An-Nisa 4:11]; he conditioned the entitlement of two-thirds on their being plural (nisa'), which is a plural, and He explicitly said 'above two, then for them is two-thirds of what he left.' That which is conditioned by a condition does not exist without it. And also because Allah gave two daughters half with the son, and he (the son) deserves half, and the share of a male is like that of two females, so it is known that the share of two daughters is half when alone. And for the majority (jumhur) is the narration from Jabir who said: The wife of Sa'd ibn al-Rabi' came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with her two daughters from Sa'd and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, these are the two daughters of Sa'd ibn al-Rabi'. Their father was martyred with you at Uhud, and their uncle took their wealth and left nothing for them; they cannot marry except with wealth.' He (the Prophet) said: 'Allah will decide regarding that.' Then the verse of inheritance was revealed. So the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent for their uncle and said: 'Give the two daughters of Sa'd two-thirds, and their mother one-eighth, and what remains is yours.' And that which was recited does not negate the entitlement of two daughters to two-thirds, because specifying something by mention does not negate the ruling from what is other than it, as is known in its place. So we know the ruling for the plural from the Book, and the ruling for the dual from the Sunnah. And also the plural may be intended for the dual, especially in inheritance, as we explained before. So the dual is intended by the verse, and that is apparent. Do you not see that when Allah explained the ruling for the plural and the dual, He made their ruling like the ruling for the plural in the case of sisters from the same parents or from the father or from the mother, in entitlement to two-thirds or one-third? And as for his saying that two daughters deserve half with the son, we say: their entitlement to that when together does not indicate their entitlement to it when alone; and the single (daughter) takes one-third with the son when alone.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage establishes that two or more daughters inherit two-thirds collectively, not half. This is the position of the majority of Companions and later scholars. It refutes the opinion of Ibn Abbas, who held that two daughters get only half based on the wording of the Quran (using 'above two' for two-thirds). The Hanafi response argues that the dual is included in the plural, and that the Prophet himself gave two daughters two-thirds in the story of Sa'd's daughters. The passage also addresses an objection that when a son is present, two daughters get half (because the son takes half and his share is like that of two females, so the daughters' collective share is half). The response explains that this is due to the presence of the son, not their independent share. So two daughters alone get two-thirds.

Key Terms
المثنى (al-muthanna): The dual number in Arabic grammar; the Hanafis argue that the Quranic plural can include the dual.
تثنية (tathniyah): The dual form; the Hanafi position holds that 'nisa' (women) in the verse includes two women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what share do two daughters of the deceased receive if there is no son?
A) One-half
B) One-third
C) Two-thirds
D) Entire estate

Key Takeaway
Two or more daughters inherit two-thirds; the Quranic plural includes the dual, and the Prophet's explicit Sunnah confirms this ruling.

Son as 'Asaba for Daughters: The Rule of Ta'sib
States the rule of ta'sib for daughters when a son is present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three states of a daughter's inheritance share and apply the rule that a son makes daughters 'asaba, giving the male double the female's share.

Core Idea
When sons and daughters inherit together, daughters become residuary and the son gets twice the share of a daughter.

In the science of faraid, a daughter's inheritance share depends on the presence of other heirs. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key rule: when a son is present, the daughter's status changes from a fixed-share heir (sahib fard) to a residuary heir ('asaba bi-ghayriha). The son, as 'asaba bi-nafsihi, makes the daughter 'asaba, and the estate is divided per capita with the male taking twice the share of each female.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three states of a daughter's inheritance
From the passage, a daughter can inherit in three ways: half if alone, two-thirds if two or more without a son, and as 'asaba when mixed with males. Note the third state is the focus of this lesson.
These states are fixed in the Quran and sunnah.
2
Understand the concept of ta'sib
Ta'sib means making someone an 'asaba. Here, the son makes the daughter an 'asaba bi-ghayrihi. This changes her from a fixed-share heir to a residuary heir who shares the residue.
The term 'asaba refers to male agnates who inherit the residue.
3
Apply the rule to a concrete scenario
For example, if a deceased leaves a son and a daughter, the estate is divided into three shares: the son gets two shares, the daughter gets one share. This fulfills the principle 'the male gets the share of two females'.
This ratio applies regardless of the number of sons and daughters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وعصبهما الابن وله مثل حظهما معناه إذا اختلط البنون والبنات عصب البنات فيكون للابن مثل حظهما فصار للبنات ثلاثة :أحوال النصف للواحدة والثلثان للاثنين فصاعداً، والتعصيب عند الاختلاط بالذكور .
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: And the son is their 'asaba, and he has the like of the share of two females. Its meaning: when sons and daughters mix, the son makes the daughters 'asaba, so the son gets the like of the share of two females. So for daughters there are three states: half for one, two-thirds for two or more, and being made 'asaba when mixed with males.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage explains that when a son is present with daughters, the daughters become 'asaba bi-ghayrihim (residuary through others), and the son takes a double share relative to each daughter (male gets twice the female). The commentary summarizes the three states of a daughter: half if alone, two-thirds if two or more without a son, and asabah (residue) when a son is present.

Key Terms
تعصيب (ta'sib): Making someone an 'asaba; here the daughter becomes 'asaba bi-ghayriha due to the son.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a deceased leaves a son and a daughter, how is the estate distributed?
A) Son gets half, daughter gets half.
B) Son gets two-thirds, daughter gets one-third.
C) Son gets twice the daughter's share.
D) Daughter gets her prescribed half, son gets residue.

Key Takeaway
A daughter's share changes from a fixed share to a residuary share when a son is present, with the son receiving twice her portion.

Children of a Son in Inheritance: Substitution, Blocking, and Residue
Inheritance rules for grandchildren through a son.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for grandchildren through a son, identify when they are blocked by a direct son, and calculate the distribution when a daughter and grandchildren coexist.

Core Idea
Children of a son inherit in place of the son, but are blocked by him; with a daughter, the closest male grandson takes the residue.

This lesson explains the Hanafi rules for the children of a son (walad al-ibn) – the grandchildren from the male line. When the son predeceases, his children step into his inheritance shoes: males become 'asaba like sons, and females receive prescribed shares like daughters. However, the presence of a living direct son blocks these grandchildren entirely. Additionally, when the deceased leaves a direct daughter and grandchildren through a son, the closest male descendant among the grandchildren inherits the residue after the daughter's half.

Guided Path
1
Identify the substitution rule
Understand that children of a son (both male and female) stand in the place of the son when the son is absent. Males are 'asaba, females get prescribed shares (1/2 if one, 2/3 if two or more) and become 'asaba with a male counterpart.
This substitution only applies to grandchildren through the son, not the daughter.
2
Apply the blocking rule
Recognize that the presence of a direct son completely blocks all children of that son, regardless of gender. The son is closer, and the grandchildren are connected through him.
The blocking is total: no prescribed share nor 'asabah.
3
Distribute when a daughter is present
If the deceased has a direct daughter and children of a son, the daughter takes her prescribed share (1/2 if alone). The closest male descendant among the grandchildren (e.g., a grandson) takes the residue as 'asaba.
If there are multiple grandchildren, only the closest male gets the residue; more distant ones are blocked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وولد) الابن كولده عند عدمه أي عند عدم الابن حتى يكون ينو الابن عصبة كالبنتين وبنات الابن كالبنات حتى يكون للواحدة النصف والبنتين فصاعداً الثلثان فيعصبهن الذكر عند اختلاطهن بالذكور فيكون للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين. قال رحمه الله : ويحجب (بالابن أي ولد الابن يحجب بالابن ذكورهـم وأناثهم فيه سواء لأن الابن أقرب وهم عصبة فلا يرثون معه بالعصوبة، وكذا بالفرض لأن بنات الابن يدلين به فلا يرثن مع الابن وإن كن لا يدلين به فإن كان عمهن فهو مساو لأصلهن فيحجبهن كما يحجب أولاده لأن ما ثبت لأحد المثلين ثبت لمساويه ضرورة. قال رحمه الله : (ومع البنت لأقرب الذكور الباقي أي إذا كان مع بنت الميت الأصلية أولاد الابن أو أولاد ابن الابن وإن سفل أو المجموع كان الباقي بعد فرض البنت الصلبية لأقرب لأنه عصبة فيحجب الأبعد وأطلق في الذكور والمراد أولاد الابن وهذا الذكور منهم
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And the child of a son is like his child when he is absent) i.e., when the son is absent, so that the sons of a son are 'asaba like the sons, and the daughters of a son are like the daughters, so that for one (daughter of a son) is half, and for two or more is two-thirds, and the male makes them 'asaba when they mix with males, so the male gets the like of the share of two females. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: And they are blocked by the son, i.e., the child of a son is blocked by the son, both their males and females equally, because the son is closer, and they are 'asaba, so they do not inherit with him by way of 'asabah; similarly by way of prescribed share, because the daughters of a son are connected through him, so they do not inherit with the son, even if they are not connected through him? For if their uncle (the son) is equal to their origin (the son), he blocks them just as he blocks his own children, because what is established for one of two equals is established for his equal necessarily. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And with the daughter, the closest male gets the residue) i.e., if with the original daughter of the deceased there are children of a son or children of a son of a son, even if low, or the combination, the remainder after the prescribed share of the direct daughter is for the closest (male), because he is 'asaba, so the further one is blocked. And he spoke generally regarding males, but the intended meaning is the children of a son, and these are the males among them.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage presents three interrelated rulings regarding children of a son (grandchildren through a son). First, in the absence of a direct son, grandchildren through a son take the place of that son: the males are 'asaba like sons, and females get half (if one) or two-thirds (if two or more) like daughters. When a male child of a son is present, females become 'asaba with him. Second, the presence of a direct son blocks all children of a son, both males and females, because the son is the closer agnate. Third, when the deceased has a direct daughter (from himself) and children of a son, the closest male descendant of the son takes the residue after the daughter's half (or half? Actually the daughter's share is half if alone). The male children of a son are 'asaba and take what remains after the daughter's prescribed share.

Key Terms
ولد الابن (walad al-ibn): Children of a son (grandchildren through the son's line); they inherit if the son is deceased.
حجب بالابن (hajb bi al-ibn): Being blocked by the son; children of a son are blocked by the direct son.
عصبة (asaba): Agnatic heir who inherits the residue after prescribed shares, or the entire estate if no fard heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man dies leaving a son and a grandson (son's son). Who inherits?
A) Both the son and grandson inherit equally.
B) Only the son inherits; the grandson is blocked.
C) The grandson inherits half, the son half.
D) The grandson inherits two-thirds, the son one-third.

Key Takeaway
Children of a son inherit only when the direct son is absent; they are blocked by the son, and with the daughter the closest male takes the residue.

The Sixth as Completion of Two-Thirds for Granddaughters
Explains fixed share rule and hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fixed share of a son's daughter (granddaughter) when she inherits alone and explain the hadith evidence for the sixth as completion of two-thirds.

Core Idea
A sole granddaughter takes half; with one daughter, she takes the sixth to complete two-thirds.

This lesson establishes the fixed share (fard) of granddaughters (بنات الابن) in Hanafi inheritance law. We examine the ruling that a single granddaughter receives half, two or more receive two-thirds, and when a direct daughter exists, the granddaughter receives the sixth to complete the two-thirds. The foundation is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, which we analyze in detail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two states of granddaughters
The text states that granddaughters have two states: they either take a fixed share (half or two-thirds) when no male in their degree, or they become 'asabah with a male. Here we focus on the first state.
2
Understand the completion (takmilah) concept
Allah prescribed two-thirds for female children. A direct daughter takes half, so the sixth remains to complete two-thirds. The granddaughter takes that sixth as 'takmilah', evidence she is included in 'children'.
3
Analyze the hadith proof from Ibn Mas'ud
Ibn Mas'ud reports the Prophet ﷺ said: 'For the daughter is half, for the son's daughter is the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds, and the remainder is for the sister.' This hadith directly establishes the sixth share.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear and accepted by the majority.
4
Note the majority adoption
The text mentions that this is the school of 'Ali, Zayd, and the generality of scholars, indicating the relied-upon position.
Ibn Mas'ud held a different view, which will be discussed next.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كَانَتْ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ وَحُجِبْنَ بِبِنْتَيْنِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ أَوْ أَسْفَلَ مِنْهُنَّ ذَكَرٌ فَيُعَصِّبُ مَنْ بِحِذَائِهِ وَمَنْ كَانَتْ فَوْقَهُ مِمَّنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ ذَاتَ سَهْمٍ وَيَسْقُطُ مِنْ دُونَهُ. قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ: (وَلِلْإِنَاثِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ) وَمُرَادُهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي دَرَجَتِهِنَّ ابْنُ ابْنٍ وَأَمَّا إِذَا كَانَ مَعَهُنَّ ابْنُ ابْنٍ يَكُنَّ عَصَبَةً مَعَهُ فَلَا يَرِثْنَ السُّدُسَ وَإِنَّمَا كَانَ لَهُنَّ السُّدُسُ عِنْدَ انْفِرَادِهِنَّ لِقَوْلِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ فِي بِنْتٍ وَبِنْتِ ابْنٍ وَأُخْتٍ : سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ : لِلْبِنْتِ النِّصْفُ وَلِبِنْتِ الابْنِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ وَالْبَاقِي لِلْأُخْتِ. فَبَنَاتُ الابْنِ لَهُنَّ حَالَانِ: سَهْمٌ وَتَعْصِيبٌ. إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْمَيِّتِ ابْنٌ وَلَا ابْنَتَانِ فَصَاعِدًا وَلَا ابْنُ ابْنٍ فَهِيَ صَاحِبَةُ سَهْمٍ وَسَهْمُ الْوَاحِدَةِ النِّصْفُ وَالثِّنْتَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا فَهُنَّ صَاحِبَاتُ الثُّلُثَيْنِ حَيْثُ لَا ذَكَرَ فِي دَرَجَتِهِنَّ وَلَا يَزِدْنَ عَلَى الثُّلُثَيْنِ وَإِنْ كَثُرْنَ، هَذَا قَوْلُ الصَّحَابَةِ رضي الله عنهم وَعَامَّةِ الْفُقَهَاءِ. وَإِنْ كَانَ لِلْمَيِّتِ ابْنَتَانِ فَلَا شَيْءَ لِبِنْتِ الابْنِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي دَرَجَتِهَا أَوْ أَسْفَلَ مِنْهَا ابْنُ ابْنٍ فَتَصِيرُ عَصَبَةً لَهُ وَيُقْسَمُ مَا بَقِيَ مِنَ الْمَالِ بَعْدَ نَصِيبِ الابْنَتَيْنِ بَيْنَهُمَا لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ. فَقَوْلُهُ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى أَنَّهُنَّ يَدْخُلْنَ فِي لَفْظِ الْأَوْلَادِ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى جَعَلَ لِلْأَوْلَادِ الْإِنَاثِ الثُّلُثَيْنِ، فَإِذَا أَخَذَتِ الصُّلْبِيَّةُ النِّصْفَ بَقِيَ مِنْهُ السُّدُسُ فَيُعْطَى لَهَا تَكْمِلَةً لِذَلِكَ فَلَوْلَا أَنَّهُنَّ دَخَلْنَ فِي الْأَوْلَادِ وَفَرْضُهُنَّ وَاحِدٌ لَمَا صَارَ تَكْمِلَةً لَهُ إِلَّا أَنَّ الصُّلْبِيَّةَ أَقْرَبُ إِلَى الْمَيِّتِ فَيَتَقَدَّمُ عَلَيْهِنَّ بِالنِّصْفِ وَدُخُولُهُنَّ عَلَى أَنَّهُ عُمُومُ الْمَجَازِ أَوْ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ. قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ : ( وَحُجِبْنَ بِبِنْتَيْنِ) أَيْ يُحْجَبُ بَنَاتُ الابْنِ بِبِنْتَيْنِ صُلْبِيَّتَيْنِ لِأَنَّ إِرْثَهُنَّ كَانَ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ وَقَدْ كَمَلَ بِثُلُثَيْنِ فَسَقَطْنَ إِذْ لَا طَرِيقَ لِتَوْرِيثِهِنَّ فَرْضًا وَتَعْصِيبًا. قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ : (إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ أَوْ أَسْفَلَ مِنْهُنَّ ذَكَرٌ فَيُعَصِّبُ مَنْ كَانَتْ بِحِذَائِهِ وَمَنْ كَانَتْ فَوْقَهُ مِمَّنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ ذَاتَ سَهْمٍ وَيَسْقُطُ مِنْ دُونَهُ أَرَادَ بِقَوْلِهِ «مَعَهُنَّ» أَنْ يَكُونَ الْغُلَامُ فِي دَرَجَتِهِنَّ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ أَخًا لَهُنَّ أَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ وَهَذَا مَذْهَبُ عَلِيٍّ وَزَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ رضي الله عنهما وَبِهِ أَخَذَ عَامَّةُ الْعُلَمَاءِ.
They were a completion of the two-thirds and are excluded by two daughters, unless there is a male with them or below them, then he makes an 'asabah of whoever is at his level and whoever is above him from among those who do not have a fixed share, and those below him fall. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And for the females is the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds.' His intent is when there is no son's son in their degree. But if there is a son's son with them, they become 'asabah with him, so they do not inherit the sixth. They only get the sixth when alone, due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud concerning a daughter, a son's daughter, and a sister: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: 'For the daughter is half, for the son's daughter is the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds, and the remainder is for the sister.' So daughters of a son have two states: a share and ta'sib. If the deceased has no son and no two or more daughters and no son's son, then she is a sharer; the share of one is half, and two or more have two-thirds, when there is no male in their degree, and they do not exceed two-thirds even if they are many. This is the saying of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and the generality of jurists. If the deceased has two daughters, then nothing is for the son's daughter unless there is a son's son at her level or below her, then she becomes an 'asabah for him, and the remainder of the wealth after the share of the two daughters is divided between them, with the male receiving the share of two females. His saying 'completion of the two-thirds' is evidence that they are included in the word 'children' because Allah made for female children two-thirds. So when the direct daughter takes half, the sixth remains and is given to her as a completion thereof. Were it not that they are included in 'children' and their prescribed share is one, it would not be a completion for it, except that the direct daughter is closer to the deceased, so she takes precedence over them with half. Their inclusion is either as a metaphorical general meaning or by consensus. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And they are excluded by two daughters,' meaning daughters of a son are excluded by two direct daughters because their inheritance was a completion of the two-thirds, and it has been completed by two-thirds, so they fall, as there is no way to give them inheritance by fixed share or ta'sib. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'Unless there is a male with them or below them, then he makes an 'asabah of whoever is at his level and whoever is above him from among those who do not have a fixed share, and those below him fall.' He meant by his saying 'with them' that the boy is at their level, whether he is their brother or not. This is the school of 'Ali and Zayd ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them, and the majority of scholars adopted it.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This lesson is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the inheritance of granddaughters (بنات الابن). The text begins by stating that granddaughters receive the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds, and they are excluded by two daughters unless there is a male (son's son) with them or below them, in which case he makes them 'asabah. The author then quotes the matn: 'And for the females is the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds.' The commentary explains that this applies when there is no son's son in their degree. If there is a son's son, they become 'asabah with him and do not take the sixth. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet ﷺ assigned half to the daughter, sixth to the granddaughter, and remainder to the sister. The text further elaborates that granddaughters have two states: either they take a fixed share (half for one, two-thirds for two or more) when alone, or they become 'asabah with a male. They are excluded by two direct daughters because their share was a completion of the two-thirds, which is now fulfilled. However, if there is a male (son's son) in their degree or below, he makes them 'asabah, and they share the remainder after the daughters' shares, with the male taking double. This is the view of 'Ali and Zayd ibn Thabit, adopted by the majority.

Key Terms
بَنَات الابْن (banāt al-ibn): Granddaughters through the son (son's daughters).
تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ (takmilatan lil-thuluthayn): The sixth share given to granddaughters to complete the two-thirds that would have gone to daughters.
حَجْب (hajb): Exclusion from inheritance by a closer heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When do granddaughters (بنات الابن) receive the sixth share (السدس)?
A) When there are two direct daughters and no male in their degree
B) When there is no male in their degree and no two direct daughters
C) When there is a son's son at their level
D) Whenever there are no direct children

Key Takeaway
Granddaughters are fixed sharers: half for one, two-thirds for two or more, and the sixth when a daughter exists, as per the hadith.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
8 min
Exclusion of Granddaughters by Two Daughters and Ta'sib with a Male
Explains exclusion by daughters and ta'sib with a male.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that granddaughters are excluded by two direct daughters and explain how a male (son's son) makes them 'asabah.

Core Idea
Two direct daughters exclude granddaughters entirely unless a male makes them 'asabah.

This lesson examines the conditions under which granddaughters are excluded from inheritance. The text explains that when the deceased has two or more direct daughters, the granddaughters are blocked because the two-thirds is already fulfilled. However, if there is a male (son's son) at their level or below, he makes them 'asabah, and they share the remainder. This is the school of 'Ali and Zayd, adopted by the majority.

Guided Path
1
Understand the exclusion rule
The text states 'they are excluded by two daughters.' Because the two-thirds is complete, there is no room for the granddaughter's share, and no ta'sib path unless a male exists.
Exclusion here is hajb hirman (total exclusion).
2
Identify the exception for ta'sib with a male
If a son's son is with them or below them, he makes the granddaughters 'asabah. They share the remainder after the daughters' shares, with the male getting double.
The male must be at the granddaughter's level or lower; if above, he is not in their degree.
3
Clarify 'with them' and 'below them'
'With them' means the male is at their same degree (e.g., brother). 'Below them' means a male from a lower generation (e.g., son's son's son). The rule differentiates: those at the same level or above who do not have a fixed share are made 'asabah; those below fall.
The text: 'يُعَصِّبُ مَنْ كَانَتْ بِحِذَائِهِ وَمَنْ كَانَتْ فَوْقَهُ مِمَّنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ ذَاتَ سَهْمٍ وَيَسْقُطُ مِنْ دُونَهُ'
4
Note the school of 'Ali and Zayd
This is the relied-upon school adopted by the generality of scholars.
The text ends by confirming this is the madhhab of 'Ali and Zayd.

سَهْمٍ وَيَسْقُطُ مِنْ دُونَهُ. قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ: (وَلِلْإِنَاثِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ) وَمُرَادُهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي دَرَجَتِهِنَّ ابْنُ ابْنٍ وَأَمَّا إِذَا كَانَ مَعَهُنَّ ابْنُ ابْنٍ يَكُنَّ عَصَبَةً مَعَهُ فَلَا يَرِثْنَ السُّدُسَ وَإِنَّمَا كَانَ لَهُنَّ السُّدُسُ عِنْدَ انْفِرَادِهِنَّ لِقَوْلِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ فِي بِنْتٍ وَبِنْتِ ابْنٍ وَأُخْتٍ : سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ : لِلْبِنْتِ النِّصْفُ وَلِبِنْتِ الابْنِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ وَالْبَاقِي لِلْأُخْتِ. فَبَنَاتُ الابْنِ لَهُنَّ حَالَانِ: سَهْمٌ وَتَعْصِيبٌ. إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْمَيِّتِ ابْنٌ وَلَا ابْنَتَانِ فَصَاعِدًا وَلَا ابْنُ ابْنٍ فَهِيَ صَاحِبَةُ سَهْمٍ وَسَهْمُ الْوَاحِدَةِ النِّصْفُ وَالثِّنْتَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا فَهُنَّ صَاحِبَاتُ الثُّلُثَيْنِ حَيْثُ لَا ذَكَرَ فِي دَرَجَتِهِنَّ وَلَا يَزِدْنَ عَلَى الثُّلُثَيْنِ وَإِنْ كَثُرْنَ، هَذَا قَوْلُ الصَّحَابَةِ رضي الله عنهم وَعَامَّةِ الْفُقَهَاءِ. وَإِنْ كَانَ لِلْمَيِّتِ ابْنَتَانِ فَلَا شَيْءَ لِبِنْتِ الابْنِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي دَرَجَتِهَا أَوْ أَسْفَلَ مِنْهَا ابْنُ ابْنٍ فَتَصِيرُ عَصَبَةً لَهُ وَيُقْسَمُ مَا بَقِيَ مِنَ الْمَالِ بَعْدَ نَصِيبِ الابْنَتَيْنِ بَيْنَهُمَا لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ. فَقَوْلُهُ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى أَنَّهُنَّ يَدْخُلْنَ فِي لَفْظِ الْأَوْلَادِ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى جَعَلَ لِلْأَوْلَادِ الْإِنَاثِ الثُّلُثَيْنِ، فَإِذَا أَخَذَتِ الصُّلْبِيَّةُ النِّصْفَ بَقِيَ مِنْهُ السُّدُسُ فَيُعْطَى لَهَا تَكْمِلَةً لِذَلِكَ فَلَوْلَا أَنَّهُنَّ دَخَلْنَ فِي الْأَوْلَادِ وَفَرْضُهُنَّ وَاحِدٌ لَمَا صَارَ تَكْمِلَةً لَهُ إِلَّا أَنَّ الصُّلْبِيَّةَ أَقْرَبُ إِلَى الْمَيِّتِ فَيَتَقَدَّمُ عَلَيْهِنَّ بِالنِّصْفِ وَدُخُولُهُنَّ عَلَى أَنَّهُ عُمُومُ الْمَجَازِ أَوْ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ. قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ : ( وَحُجِبْنَ بِبِنْتَيْنِ) أَيْ يُحْجَبُ بَنَاتُ الابْنِ بِبِنْتَيْنِ صُلْبِيَّتَيْنِ لِأَنَّ إِرْثَهُنَّ كَانَ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ وَقَدْ كَمَلَ بِثُلُثَيْنِ فَسَقَطْنَ إِذْ لَا طَرِيقَ لِتَوْرِيثِهِنَّ فَرْضًا وَتَعْصِيبًا. قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ : (إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ أَوْ أَسْفَلَ مِنْهُنَّ ذَكَرٌ فَيُعَصِّبُ مَنْ كَانَتْ بِحِذَائِهِ وَمَنْ كَانَتْ فَوْقَهُ مِمَّنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ ذَاتَ سَهْمٍ وَيَسْقُطُ مِنْ دُونَهُ أَرَادَ بِقَوْلِهِ «مَعَهُنَّ» أَنْ يَكُونَ الْغُلَامُ فِي دَرَجَتِهِنَّ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ أَخًا لَهُنَّ أَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ وَهَذَا مَذْهَبُ عَلِيٍّ وَزَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ رضي الله عنهما وَبِهِ أَخَذَ عَامَّةُ الْعُلَمَاءِ.
They were a completion of the two-thirds and are excluded by two daughters, unless there is a male with them or below them, then he makes an 'asabah of whoever is at his level and whoever is above him from among those who do not have a fixed share, and those below him fall. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And for the females is the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds.' His intent is when there is no son's son in their degree. But if there is a son's son with them, they become 'asabah with him, so they do not inherit the sixth. They only get the sixth when alone, due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud concerning a daughter, a son's daughter, and a sister: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: 'For the daughter is half, for the son's daughter is the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds, and the remainder is for the sister.' So daughters of a son have two states: a share and ta'sib. If the deceased has no son and no two or more daughters and no son's son, then she is a sharer; the share of one is half, and two or more have two-thirds, when there is no male in their degree, and they do not exceed two-thirds even if they are many. This is the saying of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and the generality of jurists. If the deceased has two daughters, then nothing is for the son's daughter unless there is a son's son at her level or below her, then she becomes an 'asabah for him, and the remainder of the wealth after the share of the two daughters is divided between them, with the male receiving the share of two females. His saying 'completion of the two-thirds' is evidence that they are included in the word 'children' because Allah made for female children two-thirds. So when the direct daughter takes half, the sixth remains and is given to her as a completion thereof. Were it not that they are included in 'children' and their prescribed share is one, it would not be a completion for it, except that the direct daughter is closer to the deceased, so she takes precedence over them with half. Their inclusion is either as a metaphorical general meaning or by consensus. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And they are excluded by two daughters,' meaning daughters of a son are excluded by two direct daughters because their inheritance was a completion of the two-thirds, and it has been completed by two-thirds, so they fall, as there is no way to give them inheritance by fixed share or ta'sib. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'Unless there is a male with them or below them, then he makes an 'asabah of whoever is at his level and whoever is above him from among those who do not have a fixed share, and those below him fall.' He meant by his saying 'with them' that the boy is at their level, whether he is their brother or not. This is the school of 'Ali and Zayd ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them, and the majority of scholars adopted it.

Commentary
This lesson is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the inheritance of granddaughters (بنات الابن). The text begins by stating that granddaughters receive the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds, and they are excluded by two daughters unless there is a male (son's son) with them or below them, in which case he makes them 'asabah. The author then quotes the matn: 'And for the females is the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds.' The commentary explains that this applies when there is no son's son in their degree. If there is a son's son, they become 'asabah with him and do not take the sixth. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet ﷺ assigned half to the daughter, sixth to the granddaughter, and remainder to the sister. The text further elaborates that granddaughters have two states: either they take a fixed share (half for one, two-thirds for two or more) when alone, or they become 'asabah with a male. They are excluded by two direct daughters because their share was a completion of the two-thirds, which is now fulfilled. However, if there is a male (son's son) in their degree or below, he makes them 'asabah, and they share the remainder after the daughters' shares, with the male taking double. This is the view of 'Ali and Zayd ibn Thabit, adopted by the majority.

Key Terms
حَجْب (hajb): Exclusion from inheritance by a closer heir.
تَعْصِيب (ta'sib): Inheriting as an 'asabah (residuary heir), taking the remainder after fixed shares.
بِحِذَائِهِ (bihidha'ihi): At his level, meaning the same generation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a son's daughter when the deceased has two direct daughters and no son's son?
A) She takes the sixth (1/6)
B) She takes nothing
C) She takes one-eighth (1/8)
D) She becomes 'asabah with the daughters

Key Takeaway
Two direct daughters exclude granddaughters entirely; a male (son's son) reverses this and makes them 'asabah.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
8 min
Ibn Mas'ud's View on Granddaughters' Inheritance: Dispute with the Majority
Presents Ibn Mas'ud's view and the majority's proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Ibn Mas'ud and the Hanafi majority regarding granddaughters' inheritance with a male, and state the Hanafi proof from Quran 4:11.

Core Idea
Ibn Mas'ud excludes granddaughters with two daughters even if a male is present; the majority gives them 'asabah with the male.

This lesson examines a classical dispute in faraid (inheritance law) between the Companion Ibn Mas'ud and the majority of scholars (including the Hanafi school). The issue is whether granddaughters (daughters of the son) can inherit alongside direct daughters when there is a male (son's son). Ibn Mas'ud held that granddaughters are excluded or get the lesser of two options, while the Hanafi school argues that the Quranic verse includes them and they become 'asabah. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your appreciation of how the Hanafi school interprets the Qur'an and distinguishes a Companion's opinion from the madhhab's established position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that granddaughters (daughters of the son) with a male (son's son) become 'asabah and share the residue after the fixed shares of direct daughters are given.
This is the majority view, supported by Quran 4:11.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Ibn Mas'ud (a Companion) held that granddaughters are excluded entirely by two direct daughters, even if a male is present. If only one direct daughter, granddaughters get the lesser of a sixth or participation with the male.
This is called 'idrar (harm) according to Ibn Mas'ud.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Ibn Mas'ud argued that granddaughters are 'daughters' and their inheritance options are either a fixed share (two-thirds) or participation, but they cannot combine both. If direct daughters take two-thirds, participation would lead to combination, which is invalid.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi majority argued that Quran 4:11 (يوصيكم الله في أولادكم...) includes grandchildren as 'children'. The verse implies that all children share the estate with the male taking double. Direct daughters take fixed shares, and the remainder goes to the 'asabah (granddaughters with their brother). This does not combine fixed share and 'asabah; they are separate.
They also used analogy: like parents/spouses, the fixed share owner leaves the picture, allowing 'asabah to take residue.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Ibn Mas'ud, granddaughters may get less or nothing; under the majority, they share the residue with the male, which may give them more than two-thirds. The practical difference is that granddaughters are not excluded when a male is present.
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.

وَرُوِيَ عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رضي الله عنه أَنَّهُ قَالَ : لِيَسْقُطْنَ بَنَاتُ الابْنِ بِبِنْتَيِ الصُّلْبِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَهُنَّ غُلَامٌ وَلَا يُقَاسِمْنَهُ. وَإِنْ كَانَتِ الْبِنْتُ الصُّلْبِيَّةُ وَاحِدَةً وَكَانَ مَعَهُنَّ غُلَامٌ كَانَ لِبَنَاتِ الابْنِ أَسْوَأُ الْحَالَيْنِ بَيْنَ السُّدُسِ وَالْمُقَاسَمَةِ فَأَيُّهُمَا أَقَلُّ أُعْطِينَ. وَتُسَمَّى هَذِهِ الْمَسَائِلُ الْإِضْرَارَ عَلَى قَوْلِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ. وَحُجَّتُهُ فِي ذَلِكَ أَنَّ بَنَاتِ الابْنِ بَنَاتٌ وَفِي مِيرَاثِهِنَّ أَحَدُ أَمْرَيْنِ إِمَّا الْفَرْضُ أَوِ الْمُقَاسَمَةُ وَفَرْضُهُنَّ الثُّلُثَانِ وَالْمُقَاسَمَةُ ظَاهِرَةٌ، وَلَيْسَ لَهُنَّ أَنْ يَجْمَعْنَ. فَإِذَا اسْتَكْمَلَتِ الْبَنَاتُ الثُّلُثَيْنِ فَلَوْ قَاسَمْنَ لَزِمَ الْجَمْعُ بَيْنَهُمَا فَلَا يَجُوزُ. وَإِذَا كَانَتِ الصُّلْبِيَّةُ وَاحِدَةً أَخَذَتِ النِّصْفَ وَبَقِيَ مِنْ فَرْضِ الْبَنَاتِ السُّدُسُ فَيَأْخُذُونَهُ إِنْ كُنَّ مُنْفَرِدَاتٍ، وَإِنْ كُنَّ مَعَ الذُّكُورِ كَانَ لَهُنَّ أَقَلُّ الْأَمْرَيْنِ مِنَ السُّدُسِ وَالْمُقَاسَمَةِ لِلتَّيَقُّنِ بِهِ وَلِئَلَّا تَأْخُذَ الْبَنَاتُ أَكْثَرَ مِنَ الثُّلُثَيْنِ وَلَا مِيرَاثَ لَهُنَّ مَعَ الصُّلْبِيَّتَيْنِ عِنْدَ الِانْفِرَادِ فَكَذَا عِنْدَ الِاجْتِمَاعِ كَالْعَمَّةِ مَعَ الْعَمِّ وَابْنِ الْأَخِ مَعَ أُخْتِهِ. وَلِلْجُمْهُورِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى {يُوصِيكُمُ اللهُ فِي أَوْلَادِكُمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ} [النساء : ١١] وَأَوْلَادُ الابْنِ أَوْلَادٌ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّا مِنْ قَبْلُ فَتَشْمَلُهُنَّ الْآيَةُ. وَقَضِيَّةُ هَذَا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمَالُ مَقْسُومًا بَيْنَ الْكُلِّ إِلَّا أَنَّا عَلِمْنَا فِي حَقِّ أَوْلَادِ الابْنِ بِأَوَّلِ الْآيَةِ وَفِي حَقِّ الصُّلْبِيَّتَيْنِ أَوِ الصُّلْبِيَّةِ الْوَاحِدَةِ بِمَا بَعْدَهَا وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ جَمْعٌ بَيْنَ الْحَقِيقَةِ وَالْمَجَازِ وَلَا شُبْهَةٌ وَإِنَّمَا هُوَ عَمَلٌ بِمُقْتَضَى كُلِّ لَفْظٍ عَلَى حِدَةٍ. وَمِنْ حَيْثُ الْمَعْنَى أَنَّ الْبَنَاتِ الصُّلْبِيَّاتِ ذَوَاتُ فَرْضٍ وَبَنَاتِ الابْنِ فِي الْحَالَةِ عَصَبَاتٌ مَعَ أَخِيهِنَّ وَصَاحِبُ الْفَرْضِ إِذَا أَخَذَ فَرْضَهُ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْبَيْنِ فَكَأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ فَصَارَ الْبَاقِي فِي الْفَرْضِ لِجَمِيعِ الْمَالِ فِي حَقِّ الْعَصَبَةِ فَتُشَارِكُهُ وَلَا يَخْرُجْنَ مِنَ الْعُصُوبَةِ كَمَا لَوِ انْفَرَدَ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ صَاحِبَ الْفَرْضِ لَوْ كَانَ غَيْرَ الْبَنَاتِ كَالْأَبَوَيْنِ وَأَحَدِ الزَّوْجَيْنِ كَانَ كَذَلِكَ فَكَذَا مَعَ الْبَنَاتِ بِخِلَافِ الْعَمَّةِ مَعَ الْعَمِّ وَبَنَاتِ الْأَخِ مَعَ أَخِيهَا لِأَنَّهُنَّ يَصِرْنَ عَصَبَةً مَعَهُمَا مُطْلَقًا سَوَاءٌ كَانَ مَعَهُنَّ صَاحِبُ فَرْضٍ أَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ فَلَا يَلْزَمُ مِنِ انْتِفَاءِ الْعُصُوبَةِ فِي مَحَلٍّ لَا يَقْبَلُهَا انْتِفَاؤُهَا فِي مَحَلٍّ يَقْبَلُهَا، وَأَخْذُهُنَّ زِيَادَةً عَلَى الثُّلُثَيْنِ لَيْسَ بِمَحْظُورٍ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُنَّ يَأْخُذْنَ بِالْمُقَاسَمَةِ عِنْدَ كَثْرَتِهِنَّ بِأَنْ تَرَكَ أَرْبَعِينَ بِنْتًا.
And it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: 'Let granddaughters be excluded by two direct daughters, even if there is a boy with them, and they do not share with him. If there is one direct daughter and there is a boy with them, then for the granddaughters is the worse of the two states between the sixth and participation, so whichever is less they are given.' These are called the cases of 'idrar (harm) according to Ibn Mas'ud. His proof is that granddaughters are daughters, and their inheritance is one of two things: either a fixed share or participation, and their fixed share is two-thirds, and participation is apparent. They cannot combine. So if the daughters have taken the full two-thirds, if they participate, they would combine, which is not permissible. If there is one direct daughter, she takes half, and from the prescribed share of daughters the sixth remains, so they take it if they are alone. But if they are with males, they take the lesser of the two: the sixth or participation, to be certain and to prevent the daughters from taking more than two-thirds. They have no inheritance with two direct daughters when alone, so likewise when in their presence, like the paternal aunt with the uncle and the son's brother with his sister. The majority's proof is His statement, the Exalted: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male is the like of the share of two females' (an-Nisa: 11). And children of the son are children as we have explained before, so the verse includes them. The implication of this is that the wealth is divided among all, except that we know concerning the children of the son by the first part of the verse, and concerning the two direct daughters or the one direct daughter by what follows it. There is no combination of literal and metaphorical meaning nor ambiguity; rather it is acting according to the import of each expression separately. In terms of meaning, the direct daughters are owners of fixed shares, while granddaughters in this situation are 'asabah with their brother. When the owner of a fixed share takes his share, he leaves the picture, as if he were not there, so the remainder becomes in the fixed share for all the wealth regarding the 'asabah, so they participate with him and do not exit from 'asabah, just as if they were alone. Do you not see that if the owner of the fixed share was other than daughters, such as the parents or one of the spouses, it would be the same? Likewise with daughters, contrary to the paternal aunt with the uncle and the son's daughter with her brother, because they become 'asabah with them absolutely, whether there is an owner of a fixed share or not. So the absence of 'asabah in a case that does not admit it does not necessitate its absence in a case that admits it. And their taking more than two-thirds is not prohibited; do you not see that they take by participation when they are many, such as if forty daughters are left?
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This lesson presents a dispute (ikhtilaf) between Ibn Mas'ud and the majority of scholars including the Hanafi school. Ibn Mas'ud held that granddaughters are totally excluded by two daughters even if there is a male (son's son) with them. If there is only one daughter, granddaughters get the lesser of the sixth or participation with the male, whichever is less. His reasoning: granddaughters are 'daughters' (بنات) and their inheritance options are either fixed share (two-thirds) or participation. They cannot combine both. If daughters have already taken two-thirds, participation would lead to a combination, which is invalid. If only one daughter, they take the sixth when alone, but if with males, they take the lesser to avoid exceeding two-thirds. The majority (including Hanafis) use the Quranic verse 4:11, which includes children of the son (grandchildren). The verse implies that all children (including grandchildren) share the estate with the male taking double. The direct daughters take fixed shares, and the remainder goes to the 'asabah (male and female grandchildren). This does not involve combining literal and metaphorical meanings; it's applying different parts of the verse. The majority also argue by analogy: just as owners of fixed shares like parents or spouses do not prevent 'asabah from sharing the residue, so too with daughters. The Hanafi position is that granddaughters become 'asabah with their brother and share the surplus after the daughters' shares, even if they get more than two-thirds. This is not prohibited, as seen in cases with many daughters (e.g., forty).

Key Terms
إِضْرَار (iḍrār): A type of inheritance case where granddaughters are given the lesser of two options to prevent them from exceeding two-thirds, according to Ibn Mas'ud.
أَسْوَأُ الْحَالَيْنِ (aswa' al-ḥālayn): The worse of the two possibilities: either the fixed share (sixth) or participation with a male, whichever is less.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main proof of the majority (including Hanafis) for granddaughters becoming 'asabah with a male?
A) The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
B) The Quranic verse 4:11 about children
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy with the paternal aunt

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that granddaughters become 'asabah with a male and inherit residue, even in the presence of direct daughters, based on Quran 4:11's inclusion of grandchildren.
