Faraid — Inheritance
beginner
6 min
The Principle of Tanzil: Hierarchy of Granddaughters in Inheritance
States the foundational rule for inheritance of granddaughters (tanzil) when there are no direct daughters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of tanzil for granddaughters and apply it to determine the shares of two granddaughters at different degrees.

Core Idea
In the absence of a daughter, the closest granddaughter inherits half; the next closest inherits a sixth.

When a person dies without a direct daughter but leaves granddaughters from a son, a special hierarchy applies. This lesson introduces the foundational rule of tanzil — positioning granddaughters in the place of daughters and granddaughters according to their closeness to the deceased. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly distributing the estate in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the absence of a direct daughter
Confirm that there is no direct daughter (بنت صلبية). This triggers the tanzil rule for granddaughters.
The rule applies 'عند عدم بنات الصلب'.
2
Determine the degrees of granddaughters
List all granddaughters and rank them by closeness to the deceased (number of generations removed). The closest (highest) is first.
Closeness is based on the number of intermediary sons.
3
Place the closest granddaughter in the daughter's position
The highest granddaughter 'ينزل منزلة البنت الصلبية' — she takes the share of a daughter, which is half if alone.
4
Place the next closest granddaughter in the granddaughter's position
The next in line takes the share of a granddaughter (i.e., the share of بنات الابن) which is a sixth as completion of two-thirds.
'والتي تليها في القرب منزلة بنات الابن'.
5
Apply the rule to determine shares
The highest gets 1/2, the next gets 1/6. Any lower granddaughters get nothing unless a male is present (as will be seen in later lessons).
The total of 1/2 + 1/6 = 2/3, leaving 1/3 for other heirs or the public treasury.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْأَصْلُ فِي بَنَاتِ الابْنِ عِنْدَ عَدَمِ بَنَاتِ الصُّلْبِ أَنَّ أَقْرَبَهُنَّ إِلَى الْمَيِّتِ يَنْزِلُ مَنْزِلَةَ الْبِنْتِ الصُّلْبِيَّةِ وَالَّتِي تَلِيهَا فِي الْقُرْبِ مَنْزِلَةَ بَنَاتِ الابْنِ وَهَكَذَا يُفْعَلُ وَإِنْ سَفَلْنَ مِثَالُهُ : تَرَكَ ثَلَاثَ بَنَاتِ ابْنٍ بَعْضُهُنَّ أَسْفَلَ مِنْ بَعْضٍ بِهَذِهِ الصُّورَةِ : ابْنٍ ابْنٍ ابْنٍ ابْنٍ ابْنٍ ابْنٍ بِنْتِ ابْنٍ بِنْتِ ابْنٍ ابْنِ ابْنٍ بِنْتِ ابْنٍ بِنْتِ ابْنٍ بِنْتِ ابْنٍ بِنْتٍ بِنْتِ ابْنٍ فَالْعُلْيَا مِنَ الْفَرِيقِ الْأَوَّلِ لَا يُوَازِيهَا أَحَدٌ فَيَكُونُ لَهَا النِّصْفُ وَالْوُسْطَى مِنَ الْفَرِيقِ الْأَوَّلِ يُوَازِيهَا مِنَ الْعُلْيَا مِنَ الْفَرِيقِ الثَّانِي فَيَكُونُ لَهَا السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةً لِلثُّلُثَيْنِ وَلَا شَيْءَ لِلسَّفْلِيَاتِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُنَّ غُلَامٌ فَيُعَصِّبُهَا وَمَنْ بِحِذَائِهَا وَمَنْ فَوْقَهَا مِمَّنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ صَاحِبَةَ فَرْضٍ حَتَّى لَوْ كَانَ الْغُلَامُ مَعَ السُّفْلَى فِي الْفَرِيقِ الْأَوَّلِ عَصَّبَهَا وَعَصَّبَ الْوُسْطَى مِنَ الْفَرِيقِ الثَّانِي وَالْعُلْيَا مِنَ الْفَرِيقِ الثَّالِثِ وَسَقَطَتِ السَّفْلِيَاتُ. وَلَوْ كَانَ الْغُلَامُ مِنَ السَّفْلِيَاتِ مِنَ الْفَرِيقِ الثَّانِي عَصَّبَهَا وَعَصَّبَ الْوُسْطَى مِنْهُ وَالْوُسْطَى وَالْعُلْيَا مِنَ الْفَرِيقِ الثَّالِثِ عَصَبَ الْجَمِيعَ غَيْرَ أَصْحَابِ الْفَرَائِضِ. وَالْمَعْنَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا أَنَّ الْعُلْيَا تَنْزِلُ مَنْزِلَةَ الْبِنْتِ وَالْبَاقِي مَنَازِلُ بَنَاتِ الابْنِ. وَلَوْ كَانَ الابْنُ مَعَ الْعُلْيَا مِنَ الْفَرِيقِ الْأَوَّلِ عَصَّبَ أُخْتَهُ وَسَقَطَتِ الْبَوَاقِي كَمَا ذَكَرْنَا فِي الْأَوْلَادِ. وَهَذَا النَّوْعُ مِنْهُ مِنْ مَسَائِلَ تُسَمَّى فِي عُرْفِ الْفَرْضِيِّينَ تَشْبِيبَ بَنَاتِ الابْنِ إِذْ ذُكِرْنَ مَعَ اخْتِلَافِ الدَّرَجَاتِ وَهُوَ إِمَّا
Then the principle regarding granddaughters when there are no direct daughters: the closest among them to the deceased takes the position of a direct daughter, and the one next in closeness takes the position of granddaughters, and so on, even if they are lower. An example: He left three granddaughters, some lower than others, in this form: son, son, son, son, son, son, son's daughter, son's daughter, son's son, son's daughter, son's daughter, son's daughter, daughter, son's daughter. So the highest of the first group has no one at her level, so she gets half. The middle of the first group is parallel to the highest of the second group, so she gets the sixth as a completion of the two-thirds, and nothing for the lowest, unless there is a boy with one of them, then he makes an 'asabah of her and those at her level and above her who do not have a fixed share. Even if the boy is with the lowest in the first group, he makes her an 'asabah and makes the middle of the second group and the highest of the third group, and the lower ones fall. If the boy is from the lower ones of the second group, he makes her an 'asabah and makes the middle of it and the middle and highest of the third group; he makes all 'asabah except the owners of fixed shares. The meaning is what we mentioned: the highest takes the position of a daughter, and the rest take the positions of granddaughters. If there is a son with the highest of the first group, he makes his sister an 'asabah, and the rest fall, as we mentioned concerning children. This type of case is called in the terminology of the faradiyyun 'tashbib of granddaughters' when they are mentioned with differing degrees, and it is either...
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This lesson presents a faraid case detailing the inheritance hierarchy among multiple granddaughters of different degrees when no direct daughter exists. The principle is that the closest granddaughter (by generation) takes the position of a direct daughter, inheriting half if alone. The next closest takes the position of a granddaughter, inheriting the sixth as completion of two-thirds. Those further down get nothing unless there is a male (son's son) who makes them 'asabah. The text gives a complex example with three levels (three 'groups') of granddaughters arranged in a diagram. The highest of the first group gets half. The middle of the first group (parallel to the highest of second group) gets the sixth. The lowest of the first group and all of the second and third groups get nothing unless a male is present. The text then elaborates scenarios where a male is with different females, making them 'asabah and excluding those below. If a son (ابن) is present with the highest granddaughter, he makes her 'asabah and all others fall. This type of case is called 'tashbib' (هذا النوع منه من مسائل تسمى في عرف الفرضيين تشبيب بنات الابن). The lesson emphasizes the hierarchical structure and the role of the male in converting fixed sharers to 'asabah.

Key Terms
تَنزِيل (tanzīl): The process of placing a granddaughter in the position of a direct daughter or granddaughter based on closeness to the deceased.

Faraid — Inheritance

Complex Granddaughter Inheritance: Applying Tanzil to Multiple Generations and the Role of Males
Presents a complex tashbib case with three groups of granddaughters and the effect of males on inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares for multiple granddaughters of different degrees and determine the effect of a male (son's son) in converting fixed sharers to 'asabah.

Core Idea
In multi-generation granddaughter cases, only the two highest-ranking females may inherit fixed shares; males at any level can make their female counterparts 'asabah and block those below.

The Hanafi school provides a detailed mechanism for distributing the estate when there are multiple granddaughters from different generations. This lesson walks through a classic tashbib case with three groups, demonstrating how the principle of tanzil applies step by step, and how the presence of a male (ghulam) or a son transforms the distribution.

Guided Path
1
Map the diagram of three groups
Identify three levels of granddaughters: highest, middle, lowest within each of three groups (generations). Understand the relationships: the middle of first group is parallel to the highest of second group, etc.
The text uses 'فريق' to denote a generation group.
2
Apply tanzil to the highest and middle of first group
The highest of first group has no parallel, so she gets half (1/2). The middle of first group is parallel to the highest of second group, so she gets the sixth (1/6) as completion of two-thirds.
Only these two receive fixed shares in the absence of a male.
3
Recognize exclusion of lower granddaughters
All lower granddaughters (سفليات) in all groups get nothing unless a male is present.
Exclusion is based on principle that only those placed in daughter/granddaughter positions inherit.
4
Introduce a male (ghulam) and analyze his effect
If a male is present with a particular granddaughter, he makes her 'asabah (عصبة) and also makes those at her level and above who are not fixed sharers 'asabah, while excluding those below.
The text gives scenarios: male with lowest of first group, male with lowest of second group.
5
Consider the case with a son (ابن)
If a son is present with the highest granddaughter, he makes her 'asabah and all other granddaughters fall (are excluded).
Because the son is closer and blocks all lower generations.
6
Understand the term tashbib
These cases are called 'تشبيب بنات الابن' (tashbib of granddaughters) when granddaughters of differing degrees are involved.
This is a specific term used by faradiyyun.

Faraid — Inheritance

Sisters as Asabah with Daughters: The Hanafi Position and Its Proof
Sharh on sisters' inheritance with daughters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a full sister inherits as an asabah with a daughter, explain the Quranic and hadith proofs, and evaluate the counterargument of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
A sister inherits with a daughter not by fixed share, but as an asabah, taking the remainder.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi faraid: when a deceased leaves a daughter, the full sister does not lose her inheritance entirely. Instead, she takes the remainder after the daughter's half share. This ruling is based on a hadith and supported by a specific interpretation of Quran 4:176, and it differs from the view of Ibn Abbas. We will walk through the evidence and the Hanafi response to the opposing argument.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the precise ruling: when a deceased leaves a daughter and a full sister, the sister inherits as an asabah (residuary) taking whatever remains after the daughter's half. This is not a fixed share but a residual inheritance.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Examine Quran 4:176 (Ayat al-Kalalah). The verse gives a sister half or two-thirds when there is 'no child' (walad). The Hanafi school argues this condition applies only to the fixed share, not to ta'sib. The sister's inheritance as asabah is not negated by the presence of a daughter.
The word 'walad' is interpreted by Hanafis as meaning male child in the context of ta'sib.
3
Understand the hadith and Companion practice
The hadith 'Make the sisters with the daughters asabah' and the practice of Mu'adh (ra) and the Prophet (pbuh) show that sisters inherit with daughters. This is stronger evidence than a literal reading of the verse.
4
Analyze Ibn Abbas's objection
Ibn Abbas (ra) argued that the presence of any child (male or female) prevents sisters from inheriting entirely, based on the condition 'not having a child' in the verse. He considered 'walad' inclusive of both sexes.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: The condition applies only to fixed-share inheritance (half or two-thirds). With a daughter, the sister inherits by ta'sib, not by fixed share. Also, the verse 'he inherits her if she has no child' refers to a male child, as the brother inherits by ta'sib only when there is no male offspring. Thus, the sister's inheritance as asabah is consistent with the Quran when properly understood.

لا تعصبهن وإنما يصرن عصبة معها لأن البنت بنفسها ليست بعصبة في هذه الحالة فكيف تعصب غيرها بخلاف الإخوة على ما يجيء عن قريب، وهذا قول جمهور الصحابة رضي الله عنهم. وروي عن ابن عباس أنه أسقط الأخوات بالنت واختلفت الرواية عنه في الإخوة والأخوات في رواية عنه الباقي كله للإخوة، وفي رواية الباقي بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين، قيل هو الصحيح من مذهبه. وكذلك لو كان البنت مع أخت لأب وأم وأخ وأخت لأب في رواية الباقي للأخ وحده، وفي رواية عنه بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين . هو احتج بقوله تعالى إن امرؤ هلك ليس له ولد وله أخت فلها نصف ما ترك [النساء : ١٧٦] فإرثها مشروط بعدم الولد واسم الولد يشمل الذكر والأنثى، ألا ترى أن الله تعالى حجب الزوج من النصف إلى الربع والزوجة من الربع إلى الثمن بالولد، والأم من الثلث إلى السدس واستوى فيه الذكر والأنثى. وللجمهور ما روينا واشترط عدم الولد فيما تلا إنما كان لإرثها النصف أو الثلثين بطريق الفرض ونحن نقول : إنها لا ترث مع البنت فرضاً وإنما ترث على أنها عصبة ويحتمل أن يراد بالولد هنا الذكر وقد قامت الدلالة على ذلك وهو قوله وهو يرثها إن لم يكن لها ولد يعني أخاها يرثها إن لم يكن لها ولد ذكر لأن الأمة اجتمعت على أن الأخ يرث تعصيباً مع الأنثى من الأولاد أو نقول : اشتراط عدم الولد إنما كان لإرث الأخ جميع مالها وذلك يمتنع بالولد وإن كان أنثى .
Like daughters of the loin when they are absent, and for the father like granddaughters with the daughters of the loin, and their asabah are their brothers. And 'sahm' is derived from saying 'tashabbaba fulan bi-fulana' if he frequently mentioned her in his poetry, and 'tashabbaba al-qasidah' by its beauty and arranges it by mentioning the building, or from 'shabba al-nar' if he kindled it. So the horse 'tashibbu shabban' if it raises both its forelegs, and 'ashbaba' I did if I helped it in that, because it is a going out and ignition. It is said 'ashabba al-nara' from a degree to another, like the state of the horse in its repetition, i.e. its young age. So for granddaughters there are six states: the three mentioned for daughters, and one-sixth with a full daughter, and exclusion by the son and by two full daughters, unless there is a male child with them. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And sisters for father and mother are like daughters of the loin when they are absent) i.e., when daughters and granddaughters are absent, so that for one there is half, for two there is two-thirds. And with brothers for father and mother, for the male the share of two females, due to His statement, Most High: 'Say, Allah gives you a ruling concerning the kalalah: If a man dies having no child and he has a sister, then for her is half of what he left, and he inherits her if she has no child. But if there are two, then for them is two-thirds of what he left. But if there are brothers and sisters, men and women, then for the male is the share of two females.' (An-Nisa 176). And we have mentioned that the sister for father and mother has two states: a share and asabah, if the deceased has no child, no grandson however low, and no grandfather (father's father) however high. And the sisters for father and mother: the share of one is half, of two or more is two-thirds, and it is not increased beyond two-thirds even if they are many. But if he has a grandfather (father's father), then the grandfather according to Abu Hanifah excludes all sisters like the father, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he does not exclude. And if the deceased has a son or a son's daughter, then the sister in this case is an asabah: she takes half? No, the granddaughter takes half as her prescribed share, so she becomes asabah with the daughter and with the granddaughter. Similarly, if there is with her a male sibling of the same degree (for father and mother) he also becomes asabah. And in al-Kafi: And with a brother for father and mother, for the male is the share of two females. And the sister for father is like the children of the son with the full daughters by consensus: for one is half, for more than one two-thirds, when there are no brothers for father and mother; and for them is one-sixth with the sister for father and mother to complete two-thirds; and for them is the remainder with daughters or with granddaughters. And in al-Zahiriyyah: And a case of inheritance of brothers and sisters: a man died leaving three different types of brothers: two brothers for father and mother, four brothers for father, four brothers for mother – then for the maternal brothers is one-third, the remainder goes to the paternal brothers, and nothing for the brothers for father. And if he left two sisters for father and mother, four sisters for father, and four brothers and four sisters for mother, according to the derivation we mentioned, then two-thirds is between the brothers and sisters for father and mother, for the male the share of two females. And if a man dies leaving a daughter or a sister for father and mother, then for the daughter is half and the remainder for the sister for father and mother by ta'sib. And if a woman dies leaving her husband and a sister for father and mother, then for the husband is half and for the sister is half by prescribed share. If there are two sisters, then for them is two-thirds, and the calculation becomes awl, and they do not get the remainder because the sister does not become an asabah except in three places: (1) sisters with daughters become asabah; (2) if a male mixes with females, they become asabah; (3) the brother with mother, father, and grandfather in the absence of father. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for the father like granddaughters with the full daughters, so that for one of the sisters for father is half when there are no sisters for father and mother, and for two is two-thirds and upwards, and with brothers for father, for the male the share of two females, and with the single sister for father and mother one-sixth to complete two-thirds for her, and they are excluded by two sisters for father and mother unless there is with them a male for father, then he makes them asabah because we recited and explained. And the dispute of Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, will come regarding the sharing of brothers after the prescribed share of the two sisters for father and mother. And the discussion about sisters is like the discussion about daughters, and the revealed text concerning them is like the revealed text concerning daughters, so we are dispensed from researching them by researching daughters, because the method of research in both is one. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And their asabah are their brothers) meaning the brothers (for father and mother or for father) make the sisters asabah, i.e., the equivalent ones, and 'brothers' is not a condition; likewise the grandfather makes them asabah in the absence of the equivalent brother, and he shares with her. In Kashf al-Ghawamid: And the full sister does not make a brother for father an asabah by consensus, because she is stronger than him in lineage; rather she takes her prescribed share, and a brother for father does not make a sister for father an asabah, indeed he excludes her because he is stronger than her by consensus. End. Its evidence is the statement of the Most High: 'But if they are brothers, men and women...' (An-Nisa 176) the verse. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the daughter and the granddaughter) meaning the daughter and granddaughter make the sisters asabah, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Make the sisters with the daughters asabah.' And Mu'adh, may Allah be pleased with him, made the daughter half and the sister half while the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was alive that day. And it is narrated that he ruled in a case of a daughter, a granddaughter, and a sister: for the daughter half, for the granddaughter one-sixth, and the remainder for the sister. And the author made the daughter one who makes sisters asabah, which is metaphorical; in reality she does not make them asabah, rather they become asabah with her, because the daughter herself is not an asabah in this case, so how can she make others asabah? Unlike brothers, as will come shortly. And this is the opinion of the majority of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. And it is narrated from Ibn Abbas that he excluded the sisters by the daughter, and the narration differs regarding brothers and sisters: in one narration, the entire remainder goes to the brothers; in another, the remainder is between them, for the male the share of two females. It is said that this is correct from his madhhab. Similarly, if there is a daughter with a sister for father and mother and a brother and sister for father, in one narration the remainder is for the brother alone, and in another narration it is between them, for the male the share of two females. He (Ibn Abbas) argued with the statement of the Most High: 'If a man dies having no child and he has a sister, then for her is half of what he left' (An-Nisa 176); so her inheritance is conditioned on the absence of a child, and the term 'child' includes male and female. Do you not see that Allah excluded the husband from half to quarter and the wife from quarter to eighth by a child, and the mother from third to sixth, and male and female are equal in that? And for the majority is what we narrated, and the condition of absence of a child in the recited verse is only for her inheritance of half or two-thirds by way of prescribed share. And we say: She does not inherit with the daughter by prescribed share; rather she inherits as an asabah. And it is possible that by 'child' here is meant the male, and the evidence for that is established: it is His statement 'and he inherits her if she has no child' meaning her brother inherits her if she has no male child, because the ummah agreed that the brother inherits by ta'sib with a female offspring. Or we say: The condition of absence of a child was only for the brother inheriting all of her wealth, and that is prevented by a child even if it is female.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqaiq, discussing the faraid (inheritance) rules for sisters. The author begins by comparing paternal sisters (for father and mother) to daughters in their shares when daughters are absent. The key ruling: a single full sister gets half, two or more get two-thirds. With a full brother, the male gets double the female's share, based on the Quranic verse 4:176. The commentary details various scenarios: when there is a grandfather (Abu Hanifa says he excludes all sisters like a father, but the Sahibayn disagree), when there is a son or granddaughter, the sister becomes an asabah. It also covers the case of three types of siblings (maternal, paternal, and full) with a practical example. The text then transitions to paternal sisters (for father only), stating they get half when no full sister, two-thirds for two or more, and one-sixth with a single full sister to complete two-thirds. They are excluded by two full sisters unless there is a paternal brother who makes them asabah. An important point: a full sister cannot make a paternal brother an asabah, and a paternal brother excludes a paternal sister. The discussion then moves to the rule that daughters and granddaughters make sisters asabah, supported by a hadith. The author notes the linguistic nuance: the daughter is not actually an asabah herself, so she cannot make others asabah; rather, the sisters become asabah alongside her. The passage then presents a significant difference from Ibn Abbas, who argued that the presence of a child (male or female) prevents a sister from inheriting altogether. The Hanafi position (based on the majority of Companions) is that the sister inherits as an asabah with the daughter, not by prescribed share. The response refutes Ibn Abbas by showing that the Quranic condition of 'no child' applies only to the fixed share inheritance, but when a daughter exists, the sister takes the remainder as an asabah. The passage includes multiple proofs and shows the depth of Hanafi faraid reasoning.

Key Terms
الأخت لأب وأم (al-ukht li-ab wa-umm): Full sister (same father and mother).
الأخت لأب (al-ukht li-ab): Paternal sister (same father, different mother).
عصبة (asabah): A residuary heir who takes the remainder after prescribed shares, or all if no others.
تعصيب (ta'sib): The process of inheriting as an asabah, taking the residual share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased leaves a daughter and a full sister. According to the Hanafi school, what does the sister inherit?
A) Nothing, because the daughter prevents inheritance.
B) Half as a fixed share.
C) The remainder as an asabah after the daughter's half.
D) One-sixth as a fixed share.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a full sister inherits as an asabah with a daughter, taking the remainder, based on the hadith 'Make the sisters with the daughters asabah' and the interpretation of Quran 4:176.

Faraid — Inheritance

Maternal Siblings' Shares in Hanafi Faraid
Matn ruling for maternal siblings' shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the shares of maternal siblings in Hanafi faraid and explain why males and females receive equal shares.

Core Idea
Maternal siblings divide equally regardless of gender — an exception to the 2:1 rule.

This lesson examines the fixed shares for maternal siblings (walad al-umm) in Islamic inheritance. The Hanafi school derives these shares from Quran 4:12, which treats them equally. Understanding this rule is essential because it is one of the few cases where males and females inherit equally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category: walad al-umm
Maternal siblings share the same mother but have different fathers. They are distinct from full and paternal siblings.
They are also called ikhwa li-umm.
2
State the share for a single maternal sibling
If there is exactly one maternal sibling, he or she receives one-sixth (1/6) of the estate.
This applies whether the sibling is male or female.
3
State the share for two or more maternal siblings
If there are two or more maternal siblings, they collectively receive one-third (1/3) of the estate.
The collective share is divided equally among all individuals.
4
Apply the equality rule
Unlike other inheritance cases, maternal siblings share equally. The gender of the sibling does not affect the portion; males and females receive identical shares.
This is a unique exception in faraid.
5
Connect to the Quranic proof
The ruling is based on Quran 4:12: 'But if he had brothers or sisters, then for each of them is one-sixth' – interpreted by the Hanafis as referring to maternal siblings, and the equality is derived from the wording and consensus.
The verse does not distinguish gender, so they are equal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وللواحد من ولد الأم السدس وللأكثر الثلث ذكورهم وأناثهم سواء)
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for the single one from the children of the mother, one-sixth, and for more than one, one-third, their males and females are equal.)
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This is a concise matn ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explained in al-Bahr al-Raiq. It addresses the inheritance of maternal siblings (those who share the same mother but different fathers). The ruling: a single maternal sibling (brother or sister) receives one-sixth of the estate. If there are two or more maternal siblings, they collectively get one-third, and they divide it equally among themselves regardless of gender. This is a unique case in Islamic inheritance where males and females receive equal shares. The proof is from the Quranic verse 4:12: 'But if he had brothers or sisters, then for each of them is one-sixth' – the verse is interpreted to apply to maternal siblings, and the equality between males and females is established by consensus and the wording of the verse. This ruling is well-established in the Hanafi school and is an important exception to the general rule that males get double the female's share.

Key Terms
ولد الأم (walad al-umm): Maternal siblings (children of the same mother but different fathers). Also known as 'ikhwa li-umm'.
السدس (al-suds): One-sixth, the prescribed share for a single maternal sibling.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third, the collective share for two or more maternal siblings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a deceased leaves two maternal brothers and one maternal sister, what share do they collectively receive?
A) One-sixth, divided equally among them.
B) One-third, divided equally among them.
C) One-third, with the brothers getting double the sister's share.
D) Half, with the brothers getting double the sister's share.

Key Takeaway
Maternal siblings inherit equally: a single sibling gets 1/6, two or more get 1/3 collectively, divided equally regardless of gender.

Faraid — Inheritance

Sisters Becoming 'Asabah with Daughters and Ibn 'Abbas' Dispute
Explains that daughters make sisters 'asabah and discusses Ibn 'Abbas' opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that sisters become 'asabah with daughters and evaluate Ibn 'Abbas' counter-argument using the distinction between fard and ta'sib.

Core Idea
A sister inherits as 'asabah with a daughter, not by fixed share, reconciling the hadith with the Quranic condition.

In inheritance law, the presence of a daughter does not exclude a full or consanguine sister; rather, it transforms her into an 'asabah. This ruling, based on a specific hadith and the practice of the Companions, was contested by Ibn 'Abbas who interpreted the Quranic 'child' to include females. Understanding the Hanafi distinction between fixed shares and residuary inheritance is key to resolving this apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school hold regarding sisters and daughters? State that sisters become 'asabah with daughters and inherit the residue.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which scholar opposes this view? Ibn 'Abbas holds that sisters are excluded entirely by a daughter.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is Ibn 'Abbas' evidence? Quran 4:176 conditions a sister's inheritance on the deceased having 'no child', and he interprets 'child' to include females.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut this? They argue the condition applies only to fixed shares (fard); sisters inherit as 'asabah by another text. Alternatively, 'child' means male child.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Under Hanafi law, a daughter and sister split the estate (half each); under Ibn 'Abbas' view, the daughter takes everything.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وإنما يصرن عصبة معها لأن البنت بنفسها ليست بعصبة في هذه الحالة فكيف تعصب غيرها بخلاف الإخوة على ما يجيء عن قريب، وهذا قول جمهور الصحابة رضي الله عنهم. وروي عن ابن عباس أنه أسقط الأخوات بالنت واختلفت الرواية عنه في الإخوة والأخوات في رواية عنه الباقي كله للإخوة، وفي رواية الباقي بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين، قيل هو الصحيح من مذهبه. وكذلك لو كان البنت مع أخت لأب وأم وأخ وأخت لأب في رواية الباقي للأخ وحده، وفي رواية عنه بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين . هو احتج بقوله تعالى إن امرؤ هلك ليس له ولد وله أخت فلها نصف ما ترك [النساء : ١٧٦] فإرثها مشروط بعدم الولد واسم الولد يشمل الذكر والأنثى، ألا ترى أن الله تعالى حجب الزوج من النصف إلى الربع والزوجة من الربع إلى الثمن بالولد، والأم من الثلث إلى السدس واستوى فيه الذكر والأنثى. وللجمهور ما روينا واشترط عدم الولد فيما تلا إنما كان لإرثها النصف أو يكن لها ولد ذكر لأن الأمة اجتمعت على أن الأخ يرث تعصيباً مع الأنثى من الأولاد أو نقول : اشتراط عدم الولد إنما كان لإرث الأخ جميع مالها وذلك يمتنع بالولد وإن كان أنثى .
And the daughter and the son's daughter: for one of the children of the mother one-sixth, and for more than one one-third, their males and females equal like the portion of two females. And with the single full sister, for her one-sixth as completion of two-thirds, and they (the half-sisters) are excluded by two full sisters unless there is with them a paternal brother who makes them 'asabah. As we have recited and explained, and there will come in them the dispute of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) regarding the division of brothers after the fixed share of the two full sisters. And the discussion about sisters is like the discussion about daughters, and the text (Quran) regarding them is like the text regarding daughters, so we are dispensed from research about them by research about daughters because the method of research in both is one. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And their brothers make them 'asabah). He means brothers make the sisters for father and mother or for father only 'asabah, meaning the male parallel to them, and 'brothers' is not a restriction. Likewise, the grandfather makes them 'asabah when there is no brother parallel to them, and he divides with her. And in Kashf al-Ghawamid: And the full sister does not make the paternal brother 'asabah by consensus because she is stronger than him in lineage; rather she takes her fixed share, and the full brother does not make the paternal sister 'asabah but excludes her because he is stronger than her by consensus. End. Its evidence is His statement, exalted: 'If they are brothers, men and women...' [al-Nisa: 176]. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the daughter and son's daughter). He means the daughter and son's daughter make the sisters 'asabah due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Make the sisters with the daughters 'asabah.' And Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him) gave the daughter half and the sister half while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was alive that day. And it is narrated that he ruled concerning a daughter, a son's daughter, and a sister: for the daughter half, for the son's daughter one-sixth, and the remainder for the sister. And the author made the daughter one of those who make sisters 'asabah, and it is a metaphor; in reality she does not make them 'asabah, but rather they become 'asabah with her because the daughter herself is not an 'asabah in this case, so how can she make others 'asabah? Unlike brothers, as will come shortly. And this is the saying of the majority of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. And it is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas that he dropped the sisters with the daughter, and the narration from him differed concerning brothers and sisters: in one narration, all the remainder is for the brothers, and in another narration, the remainder is between them, the male having the portion of two females. It is said that this is the correct view of his madhhab. Likewise, if there is a daughter with a full sister and a paternal brother and sister, in one narration the remainder is for the brother alone, and in another narration, it is between them, the male having the portion of two females. He (Ibn 'Abbas) argued with His statement: 'If a man dies having no child and he has a sister, for her is half of what he left' [al-Nisa: 176]; so her inheritance is conditioned on the absence of a child, and the term 'child' includes male and female. Do you not see that Allah excluded the husband from half to quarter and the wife from quarter to eighth by the child, and the mother from one-third to one-sixth, and the male and female are equal in that? And the majority (argue) with what we narrated, and the condition of absence of a child in the recited verse was only for her inheritance of half or two-thirds by way of fard; and we say: she does not inherit with the daughter as a fard, but rather she inherits as an 'asabah. And it is possible that 'child' here means a male child, and the indication for that has been established, which is His statement: 'And he inherits from her if she has no child' [al-Nisa: 176], meaning her brother inherits from her if she has no male child, because the ummah agreed that the brother inherits by ta'sib with a female child. Or we say: the condition of absence of a child was only for the brother inheriting all her wealth, and that is prevented by a child even if it is female.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether sisters (full or consanguine) inherit as 'asabah when there is a daughter or son's daughter. The author explains the Hanafi position: sisters become 'asabah with daughters, taking the remainder after the daughters' fixed shares, based on the hadith 'Make the sisters with the daughters 'asabah' and the practice of Mu'adh and the ruling of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the case of a daughter, son's daughter, and sister. The author clarifies that the daughter herself is not an 'asabah; rather, the sisters become 'asabah alongside her, taking the residue by ta'sib. This is the view of the majority of Companions. Ibn 'Abbas held that sisters are excluded entirely by a daughter, relying on the Quranic condition that a sister inherits only if there is no child, interpreting 'child' to include females. The Hanafi response distinguishes between inheritance by fard (fixed share) and by ta'sib: the Quranic condition of no child applies to the fixed share (half or two-thirds), but when a daughter exists, the sister does not take a fixed share but rather becomes an 'asabah by another textual evidence (the hadith). Alternatively, 'child' in the verse may refer specifically to a male child, as indicated by the brother's inheritance being conditioned on no male child. Thus, the Hanafi position harmonizes the proofs.

Key Terms
عصبة (‘asabah): Residuary heir who takes the remainder after fixed shares are distributed, or the entire estate if no fixed shareholders.
تعصيب (ta‘ṣīb): The act of making someone an 'asabah, i.e., entitled to the residue.
فرض (farḍ): A fixed share prescribed in the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a man dies leaving a daughter and a full sister, how does the Hanafi madhhab distribute the estate?
A) The daughter gets half, the sister gets one-sixth as a fixed share, and the remainder goes to other heirs.
B) The daughter gets half, and the sister gets the remaining half as an 'asabah.
C) The daughter gets the entire estate, and the sister is excluded.
D) The daughter gets half, the sister gets nothing, and the residue goes to the Bait al-Mal.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance, a sister becomes an 'asabah with a daughter, inheriting the residue based on the hadith, reconciling the Quranic condition by restricting it to fixed shares.

Shares of Maternal Siblings and Their Exclusion (Hajb) in Hanafi Faraid
Sets shares for maternal siblings and explains who excludes them, with discussion on kalalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fixed shares for maternal siblings (one-sixth for one, one-third for more) and identify which heirs (son, son's son, father, grandfather) totally exclude them from inheritance.

Core Idea
Maternal siblings inherit one-sixth (single) or one-third (multiple) equally, but are totally excluded by any child or parent.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the Quranic basis for maternal siblings' shares and explains the crucial rules of exclusion (hajb). Understanding when maternal siblings inherit is key to accurate faraid calculations, as their presence or absence alters the shares of other heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for maternal siblings
Read the first sentence of the source: 'For one of the children of the mother one-sixth, and for more than one one-third, their males and females are equal.' Note that the shares are fixed and equal regardless of gender.
The Quranic verse (4:12) is cited as proof.
2
Understand the condition of kalalah
Maternal siblings inherit only when the deceased is kalalah, i.e., has no parent or child. Identify from the text the four heirs that exclude them: son, son's son (however low), father, and grandfather (however high).
Exclusion is total (hajb hirman).
3
Distinguish maternal from other siblings
Note that the daughter excludes maternal siblings but does NOT exclude full or consanguine siblings. The text explains that full/consanguine siblings have an alternative right via ta'sib (residuary) with daughters, while maternal siblings have no such alternative.
This is a critical distinction in Hanafi law.
4
Analyze the worked example from al-Mudmarat
Follow the detailed case: a man leaves two paternal cousins, one of whom is also a maternal brother. The maternal brother takes his fard (one-sixth) and then the remainder is divided as ta'sib between the two cousins equally. Understand how the original case (asl 6) is corrected to 12.
This shows how maternal siblings can also inherit as 'asabah in specific scenarios (here, through paternal cousin relationship).
5
Summarize the five states for full sisters, seven for consanguine, three for maternal
The passage ends with a comprehensive listing. Memorize the number of states for each sibling category and the key conditions affecting each.
This is an important consolidation for faraid problem-solving.

قال رحمه الله : (وللواحد من ولد الأم السدس وللأكثر الثلث ذكورهم وأناثهم سواء) كقوله تعالى وإن كان رجل يورث كلالة أو امرأة وله أخ أو أخت فلكل واحد منهما السدس فإن كانوا أكثر من ذلك فهم شركاء في الثلث [النساء : ۱۲] والمراد به أولاد الأم لأن أولاد الأم والأب مذكورون في آية النصف على ما ذكرنا من قبل ولهذا قرأها بعضهم «وله أخ أو أخت لأم وإطلاق الشركة يقتضي المساواة كما إذا قال شريكي فلان في هذا المال أو قال له شركة لأن الله تعالى سوى بينهما حالة الانفراد فدل ذلك على استوائهما على حالة الاجتماع. وفي المضمرات ولو ترك ابني عم أحدهما أخ لأم فله السدس والباقي بينهما وصورته أن يكونوا إخوة لأم و أب أو من اثني عشرة، وللأخ من الأم سبعة سهمان فرض وخمسة بالتعصيب. قال رحمه الله : وحجبن بالابن وابنه وإن سفل وبالأب وبالجد) أي الأخوات كلهن يحجبن بهؤلاء المذكورين وهم الابن وابن الابن وإن سفل، والأب والجد وإن علا، وكذا الإخوة يحجبون بهم لأن ميراثهم مشروط بالكلالة. واختلفوا في الكلالة هل هي صفة للميت أو للورثة أو للتركة وقرئ يورث» بكسر الراء وفتحها وأياماً كان يشترط لتسميته به عدم الوالد والولد للميت فيسقطون والكلالة مشتقة بهم . من الإحاطة ومنه الإكليل لاحاطته بالرأس وكذا الكلالة . من أحاط بالشخص من الإخوة الأخوات فقيل أصلها من البعد يقال كلت الرحم بين فلان وفلان إذا تباعدت، ويقال حمل فلان على فلان ثم كل عنه أي تركه وبعد عنه وغيره قرابة الولاء بعيدة بالنسبة إلى الولاد قال الفرزدق في شعر : ورثـتـم قـناة المجد لا كلالة عن عن أبي مناف عبد شمس وهاشم قال رحمه الله : (والبنت تحجب ولد الأم فقط يعني البنت تحجب الإخوة والأخوات من الأم ولا تحجب الإخوة والأخوات من الأبوين أو من الأب لأن شرط إرث ولد الأم الكلالة ولا كلالة مع الولد والبنت ولد فتحجبهم، وكذا بنت الابن لأن ولد الابن يقوم مقامه. فإن قيل : وجب أن لا ترث الإخوة والأخوات لأب وأم أو لأب فقط مع البنت وبنت الابن لأن شرط إرثهم الكلالة. قلنا : الكلالة شيء شرطت في حق ارثهن النصف أو الثلثين ولا ترث الكل بالعصوبة، فإذا انتفت الكلالة انتفى He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And for one of the children of the mother one-sixth, and for more than one one-third, their males and females are equal). Like His statement, exalted: 'And if a man is inherited from kalalah or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, for each one of them is one-sixth; and if they are more than that, they are partners in one-third' [al-Nisa: 12]. And by it is meant the children of the mother, because the children of the mother and father are mentioned in the verse of half as we mentioned before. For this reason, some recited it as 'and he has a brother or a sister from the mother.' And the unrestricted partnership implies equality, just as if someone said 'my partner so-and-so in this wealth' or said 'he has a partnership with him,' because Allah made them equal in the case of singularity, indicating their equality in the case of plurality. And in al-Mudmarat: If a man leaves two paternal cousins, one of whom is a maternal brother, then for him is one-sixth and the remainder is between them. Its form is that they are brothers from mother and father or from father only, and each of them has a wife and a son from her. Then the elder divorced his wife or she died, and the younger married her, and she gave birth to two sons. Then the younger died, then the elder, then the elder's son died. So he dies leaving two paternal cousins, one of whom is a maternal brother. The original basis of the case is from six, and it is corrected to twelve. For the maternal brother, seven shares: two shares by fard and five by ta'sib. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And they are excluded by the son, his son even if descending, by the father, and by the grandfather) meaning all sisters are excluded by these mentioned, which are: the son, the son's son even if descending, the father, and the grandfather even if ascending. Likewise, brothers are excluded by them because their inheritance is conditional on kalalah. And they differed concerning kalalah: is it a description of the deceased, or of the heirs, or of the estate? And it is recited 'yūrathu' with kasr of the ra' and with fath, and in any case, its condition is the absence of a parent and a child for the deceased, so they (siblings) are excluded. And 'kalalah' is derived from 'ihata' (encompassing), and from it is 'ikliil' (crown) because it encompasses the head, and likewise 'kalalah' from encompassing the person by brothers and sisters. It is said its origin is from distance: it is said 'kalat al-rahim' (the womb became distant) between so-and-so and so-and-so when it becomes distant. And it is said 'he carried so-and-so then kalla 'anhu' meaning he left him and became distant. And other than that, the kinship of patronage is distant compared to lineage. Al-Farazdaq said in poetry: 'You inherited the spear of glory, not by kalalah, from Ibn Manaf, 'Abd Shams and Hashim.' He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the daughter excludes the child of the mother only) meaning the daughter excludes the brothers and sisters from the mother, and does not exclude the brothers and sisters from both parents or from the father, because the condition for the inheritance of the child of the mother is kalalah, and there is no kalalah with a child, and the daughter is a child, so she excludes them. Likewise, the son's daughter because the son's child stands in his place. If it is said: It must be that the brothers and sisters from father and mother or from father only do not inherit with the daughter and son's daughter because their condition is kalalah. We say: Kalalah is a condition only for their inheritance of half or two-thirds; they do not inherit everything by 'asabah. So when kalalah is absent, this inheritance conditional on it is absent, but they become entitled to inheritance conditional on 'asabah with the daughter by another text, as we explained, unlike the children of the mother, for all of their inheritance is conditional on kalalah, so it is absent with its absence. Thus, for full brothers and sisters there are five states: half for one sister, two-thirds for more, ta'sib by their brother, ta'sib with daughters, and exclusion with the son. For paternal sisters there are seven states: the five mentioned, plus one-sixth with one full sister, and exclusion by two full sisters, as previously. And for maternal sisters there are three states: one-sixth for one, one-third for more.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the shares of maternal siblings (those from the same mother only) and the rules for their exclusion (hajb). The author first states the ruling: one maternal sibling (brother or sister) gets one-sixth, and two or more get one-third, equally between males and females. The proof is Quran 4:12, which mentions siblings in the context of kalalah, interpreted to refer to maternal siblings because full and consanguine siblings are covered in the later verse 4:176. The passage then explains that maternal siblings are excluded by the son, son's son, father, and grandfather, because their inheritance is conditional on the deceased being kalalah (having no parent or child). A detailed discussion of the linguistic and technical meaning of 'kalalah' follows, including its derivation and the different readings of the verse. The key point is that the daughter excludes only maternal siblings, not full or consanguine siblings. This is because the condition of kalalah applies to all fixed shares of siblings, but full and consanguine siblings have an alternative means of inheritance via ta'sib with daughters, whereas maternal siblings have no such alternative. The passage concludes by summarizing the various states for full sisters, consanguine sisters, and maternal sisters, listing the different shares and conditions for each category.

Key Terms
كلالة (kalālah): The state of a deceased who leaves no parent (ascendant) and no child (descendant).
ولود الأم (awlād al-umm): Children of the mother only, i.e., uterine siblings sharing the same mother but different father.
حجب (ḥajb): Exclusion from inheritance, either total (hirman) or partial (nuqsan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased woman leaves a mother, a daughter, and a full sister. According to Hanafi law, what shares do they receive?
A) Mother gets one-sixth, daughter gets half, full sister gets one-sixth as fard.
B) Mother gets one-sixth, daughter gets half, full sister gets the remaining one-third as 'asabah.
C) Mother gets one-sixth, daughter gets half, full sister is excluded by the daughter.
D) Mother gets one-third, daughter gets half, full sister gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
Maternal siblings inherit only in the absence of a child or parent, and they receive one-sixth (singular) or one-third (plural) equally, while full/consanguine siblings are not excluded by a daughter and inherit as 'asabah.

Faraid — Inheritance

Definition and Types of 'Asaba
Defines 'asaba and categorizes its types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the three types of 'asaba by lineage and two types by cause, and state the order of precedence among 'asaba bi-nafsihi.

Core Idea
The 'asaba takes the residue; its types depend on lineage and cause.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the estate is distributed first to fixed-share heirs (ashab al-furud), then the residue goes to 'asaba. Understanding who qualifies as an 'asaba and how they are prioritized is essential for calculating shares. This lesson defines 'asaba and breaks down its types, drawing on the authoritative commentary al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish description from definition
The text states that 'the one who takes the whole when alone or what the fixed-share heirs have left' is a description (rasm), not a definition (hadd), because one must know all heirs first. Understand this nuance.
This is a terminological precision point.
2
Identify the two overarching categories
'Asaba is divided into 'asaba by lineage (nasab) and 'asaba by cause (sabab). Memorize these two branches.
Cause-based includes emancipation and clientage.
3
Parse the three types of 'asaba by lineage
For each type, note: (1) 'asaba bi-nafsihi: male agnate with no female intermediary; (2) 'asaba bi-ghayrihi: female fixed-share heir who becomes 'asaba through a male counterpart; (3) 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi: female who becomes 'asaba alongside another female (e.g., sister with daughter).
These are the three types commonly cited.
4
Apply the order of precedence among 'asaba bi-nafsihi
The text gives the sequence: son, grandson (son's son), father, grandfather, full brother, consanguine brother, their sons, etc. Note that closeness to the deceased determines priority.
This order is critical for calculating shares.
5
Handle cases where multiple types coexist
When 'asaba of different types gather, preference is by closeness. If multiple 'asaba of same degree, inheritance is per head, not per lineage direction.
Example: full sister vs. brother's son.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعصبه أي من يأخذ الكل والاحق الابن ثم ابنه وإن سفل ثم الأب ثم أب الأب وإن والا : والسقوط كما ذكرنا . قال رحمه الله : ( وعصبه) وهي معطوف على قوله في أول الكتاب «ذو فرض فيكون معطوفاً على الخبر فيكون خبراً . قال رحمه الله : أي من يأخذ الكل) أي إذا انفرد وما أبقته أصحاب الفروض وهذا رسم وليس بحد لأنه لا بد أن يعرف الورثة كلهم ولا يعرف العصبة إلا بعد أن يعرفهم كلهم فنقول : العصبة نوعان : عصبة بالنسب وعصبة بالسبب . فالعصبة بالنسب ثلاثة أنواع : عصبة بنفسه وهو كل ذكر لا يدخل في نسبته إلى الميت أنثى، وعصبة بغيره وهل كل أنثى فرضها النصف أو الثلثان يصرن عصبة بأخواتهن كما تقدم، وعصبة مع غيره وهي كل أنثى تصير عصبة مع أنثى أخرى كالبنات مع الأخوات. والسبب نوعان : مولى العتاقة ومولى الموالاة وسيأتي بيانه وفي المضمرات والعصبة أربعة أصناف : عصبة بنفسه وهو جزء الميت وأصله وجزء أبيه وجزء جده الأقرب وعصبة بغيره وهي كل أنثى تصير عصبة بذكر يوازيها كالبنت مع الابن وفي الذخيرة وبنت الابن مع ابن الابن وكالأخت لأب وأم مع الأخ لأب وأم . وعصبة مع غيره وهي كل أنثى تصير عصبة مع أنثى أخرى كالأخوات لأب وأم أو لأب مع البنات وبنات الابن وإذا صار الشخص عصبة بغيره فذلك الغير لا يكون عصبة. فأما الكلام في العصبة بنفسها فنقول : أولى العصبات بالميراث الابن ثم ابن الابن وإن سفل ثم الأب. وفي المضمرات وإنما كان الابن أقرب من الأب وإن استويا في الجزئية وفي انعدام الواسطة لأن الجزئية للابن آخرهما أو كان قاضياً على الأول ثم الجد أب الأب وإن علا ثم الأخ لأب وأم ثم لأب وابن الأخ لأب وأم ثم ابن الأخ لأب ثم بنوهما وإن علوا على هذا الترتيب ثم مولى العتاقة وفي شرح الطحاوي : ثم عم الجد لأب وكذلك أولادهم على هذا الترتيب، ثم مولى العتاقة لأب وأم ثم عم ثم آخر العصوبة مقدم على ذوي الأرحام وفي الكافي: الأحق فرع الميت أي البنون ثم بنوهم وإن سفلوا. وفي المضمرات ولو أردت معرفة القرب فاعتبر كل نوع أصل واتصال الأخ بأخيه بواسطة واحدة واتصال العمومة بواستطين عرفنا أن الأخ أقرب من العم، وأما الكلام في العصبة بغيرها فصورتها ما ذكرنا وهو كل أنثى تصير عصبة بذكر كبنت الابن مع ابن الابن وكالأخت لأب وأم أو لأب مع أخيها. وهذا الحكم في الإخوة مع الأخوات مقصور على أخوات من جملة أصحاب الفروض وتصير عصبة بذكر يوازيها. وفي الكافي : وأما العصبة بغيره فأربع من النسوة وهن اللاتي فرضهن النصف والثلثان يصرن عصبة بأخوتهن ومن لا فرض لها من الإناث وأخوها عصبة لا تصير عصبة بأخيها كالعم والعمة فالمال كله للعم دون العمة وابن العم المال لابن العم دون الابنة وكبنت الأخت وابن الأخ المال كله لابن الأخ بيانه : إذا هلك الرجل وترك ابن أخ لأب وأم وبنت الأخ لأب وأم فالمال كله لابن الأخ ولا شيء لبنت الأخ لأنها من جملة ذوي الأرحام وليست من جملة أصحاب الفرائض فلم تصر عصبة، وأما بنت الابن فإنها تصير عصبة بذكر يوازيها وفي الذخيرة: على كل حال يوازيها وتصير عصبة بذكر أسفل منها إذا لم يصل إليها فرضها، وأما الكلام في العصبة مع غيره فصورتها كما ذكرنا وبيان ذلك من المسائل إذا هلك الرجل وترك بنتاً وأختاً لأب وأم أو لأب وأخاً كذلك فللبنت النصف والباقي بين الأخ والأخت أثلاثاً وقد قدمناه. إذا اجتمعت العصبات وبعضها عصبة بنفسها وبعضها عصبة بغيرها وبعضها عصبة مع غيرها فالترجيح منها بالقرب إلى الميت بيانه : إذا مات وترك بنتاً وأختاً لأب وأم وابن الأخ لأب فنصف المال للبنت والنصف للأخت ولا شيء لابن الأخ لأن الأخت عصبة مع البنت وهي إلى الميت أقرب من ابن الأخ ، وكذلك إذا كان مكان ابن الأخ عم طريقه ما في الناسخ. وإذا استوى ابنان في درجة من العصبات وفي أحدهما قرابة زائدة فهي أولى إلا أن يكون الأخ أقرب إلى الميت مثال القرابة الزائدة أخ لأب وأم وأخ لأب فالأخ الأب وأم أولى ومثال السبق أخر لأب وابن أخ لأب وأم فالأخ أولى لأنه أسبق إلى الميت، وإذا اجتمع عدد من العصبات فالمال بينهم على عدد رؤوسهم لا على الجهات مثاله : عشر ابن أخ وابن آخر فالمال بينهم على أحد عشر سهماً لا على سهمين هذا الذي ذكرناه كله في العصبة من جهة النسب.
And 'asaba: i.e., the one who takes the entire (inheritance) – the most entitled is the son, then his son even if descending, then the father, then the father's father even if ascending. And exclusion as we mentioned. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: ('Asaba) – it is coordinated with his statement at the beginning of the book: 'a fixed-share heir', so it is coordinated with the predicate, so it becomes a predicate. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (i.e., the one who takes the whole) i.e., when alone and what the fixed-share heirs have left. This is a description, not a definition, because it is necessary to know all the heirs, and one does not know the 'asaba except after knowing them all. So we say: 'Asaba are of two types: 'asaba by lineage and 'asaba by cause. 'Asaba by lineage are of three types: 'asaba bi-nafsihi (by himself): every male in whose relation to the deceased no female intervenes; 'asaba bi-ghayrihi (by others): every female whose share is half or two-thirds, they become 'asaba through their brothers, as previously mentioned; and 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi (with others): every female who becomes 'asaba along with another female, like daughters with sisters. The cause-based 'asaba are of two types: mawla al-'itaqa (master of emancipation) and mawla al-muwalah (master of clientage), and its explanation will come later. In al-Mudmarat: 'Asaba are four kinds: 'asaba bi-nafsihi: he is the offspring of the deceased, his root, his father's offspring, and his grandfather's nearest offspring; 'asaba bi-ghayrihi: every female who becomes 'asaba through a male equal to her, like a daughter with a son, and in al-Dhakhira, a son's daughter with a son's son, and a sister for father and mother with a brother for father and mother; 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi: every female who becomes 'asaba with another female, like sisters for father and mother or for father with daughters and son's daughters. And if a person becomes 'asaba through another, that other does not become 'asaba. As for the discussion of 'asaba bi-nafsihi, we say: The most entitled of the 'asaba to inheritance is the son, then the son's son even if descending, then the father. In al-Mudmarat: The son is closer than the father, even though they are equal in being part of the deceased and in absence of intermediary, because the son's part is the last of them or he is the judge over the first; then the grandfather (father's father) even if high; then the full brother, then the consanguine brother, then the full brother's son, then the consanguine brother's son, then their sons even if high in this order; then the mawla al-'itaqa. In Sharh al-Tahawi: then the grandfather's full paternal uncle and likewise their children in this order; then the mawla al-'itaqa for father and mother; then the paternal uncle; then the last of the 'asaba is given precedence over dhawi al-arham. In al-Kafi: The most entitled is the deceased's branch (the sons), then their sons even if descending. In al-Mudmarat: If you wish to know closeness, consider the root of each type and the connection of a brother to his brother through one intermediary, and the connection of paternal uncles through two intermediaries, we know that the brother is closer than the paternal uncle. As for the discussion of 'asaba bi-ghayrihi, its form is what we mentioned: every female who becomes 'asaba through a male, like a son's daughter with a son's son, and a sister for father and mother or for father with her brother. This ruling regarding brothers with sisters is limited to sisters among the fixed-share heirs, and they become 'asaba through a male equal to her. In al-Kafi: As for 'asaba bi-ghayrihi, there are four women: those whose fixed share is half or two-thirds, they become 'asaba through their brothers; and a female who has no fixed share and her brother is 'asaba, she does not become 'asaba through her brother, like the paternal uncle and aunt – all the wealth goes to the paternal uncle, not the aunt; and the paternal uncle's son – all the wealth goes to the paternal uncle's son, not his daughter; and the sister's daughter and the brother's son – all the wealth goes to the brother's son. Explanation: If a man dies leaving a full brother's son and a full brother's daughter, all the wealth goes to the brother's son, and nothing for the brother's daughter, because she is among dhawi al-arham, not among the fixed-share heirs, so she does not become 'asaba. As for the son's daughter, she becomes 'asaba through a male equal to her, and in al-Dhakhira: in any case, she becomes 'asaba through a male lower than her if her fixed share does not reach her. As for the discussion of 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi, its form is as we mentioned, and its clarification through cases: if a man dies leaving a daughter and a full sister or consanguine sister and a brother likewise, the daughter gets half, and the remainder is divided between the brother and sister in thirds, as we have already presented. When 'asaba gather, some being 'asaba bi-nafsihi, some 'asaba bi-ghayrihi, and some 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi, the preference among them is by closeness to the deceased. Explanation: If someone dies leaving a daughter, a full sister, and a full brother's son, half the wealth goes to the daughter, half to the sister, and nothing to the brother's son, because the sister is 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi with the daughter, and she is closer to the deceased than the brother's son. Likewise, if the brother's son is replaced by a paternal uncle, the ruling is the same as in al-Nasikh. If two 'asaba are equal in degree and one has an extra relation, that one is given preference, unless the other is closer to the deceased. Example of extra relation: a full brother and a consanguine brother – the full brother is given preference. Example of precedence: a consanguine brother and a full brother's son – the brother is given preference because he is earlier (in closeness) to the deceased. If a number of 'asaba gather, the wealth is divided among them by headcount, not by directions. Example: ten brother's sons and one other son – the wealth is divided into eleven shares, not two shares. This is all we have mentioned regarding 'asaba by lineage.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of 'asaba (residuary heirs) from the Hanafi text al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author begins by explaining the term 'asaba: it refers to the heir who takes the entirety of the estate when alone, or the residue after fixed-share heirs (ashab al-furud) receive their allotted portions. He notes that this is a descriptive definition, not a strict logical definition, because one can only identify the 'asaba after knowing all the heirs. He then categorizes 'asaba into two overarching types: those by lineage (nasab) and those by cause (sabab). By lineage, there are three types: (1) 'asaba bi-nafsihi – any male through whom the relationship to the deceased does not pass through a female (i.e., male agnates); (2) 'asaba bi-ghayrihi – females whose prescribed share is half or two-thirds, who become 'asaba through a male counterpart (e.g., a daughter becomes 'asaba through a son); (3) 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi – females who become 'asaba along with another female (e.g., a sister becomes 'asaba with a daughter). By cause, there are two: mawla al-'itaqa (a former master of an emancipated slave) and mawla al-muwalah (a client by contract). The author then cites al-Mudmarat, which presents a four-category view, and provides details on each type, including examples. The passage continues with extensive discussion of the order of precedence among 'asaba bi-nafsihi (the most entitled being the son, then grandson, then father, etc.) and includes numerous quotations from other Hanafi works (al-Dhakhira, Sharh al-Tahawi, al-Kafi) to explain the rules of closeness and exclusion. It also covers the rules for 'asaba bi-ghayrihi and ma'a ghayrihi in detail, with practical examples. For instance, when a deceased leaves a daughter and a full sister, the daughter takes half, and the sister becomes 'asaba with her, taking the remaining half along with any brothers. The passage concludes with the rule that if multiple types of 'asaba coexist, preference is by closeness to the deceased, and if several 'asaba of the same type gather, inheritance is divided per head, not per lineage direction. This is a comprehensive lesson on the classification and rules of 'asaba, which is foundational for inheritance calculations.

Key Terms
عصبة (ʻaṣaba): A residuary heir who takes the entire inheritance when alone, or the residue after fixed-share heirs have been allotted their shares. The term is derived from the idea of encompassing or wrapping.
عصبة بنفسه (ʻaṣaba bi-nafsihi): Every male relative whose lineage to the deceased contains no female intermediary. These are the primary 'asaba and include sons, grandsons, father, grandfather, brothers, uncles, etc.
عصبة بغيره (ʻaṣaba bi-ghayrihi): A female who becomes a residuary heir through a male counterpart of the same degree, such as a daughter with a son, or a sister with a brother. She transitions from fixed-share heir to 'asaba when accompanied by an equal or higher male relative.
عصبة مع غيره (ʻaṣaba maʻa ghayrihi): A female who becomes a residuary heir alongside another female, such as a sister inheriting 'asaba together with a daughter. The sister does not take through a male counterpart but through the presence of another female who consumes the fixed shares, leaving residue.
ذو فرض (dhū farḍ): A fixed-share heir; one who is entitled to a specific Quranic fraction of the inheritance (e.g., 1/2, 1/4, 1/8, etc.).
مولى العتاقة (mawlā al-ʻitāqah): The former master who emancipated a slave; he becomes an 'asaba by cause and inherits from the freed slave if the latter has no agnatic heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following describes an 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi?
A) A daughter inheriting 'asaba alongside a son.
B) A full sister inheriting 'asaba alongside a daughter.
C) A son inheriting 'asaba bi-nafsihi.
D) A mother inheriting a fixed share.

Key Takeaway
The 'asaba are classified into three types by lineage and two by cause; understanding their definitions and order is essential for correct inheritance distribution.

Types and Priority of Agnatic Heirs (عصبة)
Explaining types of agnates and their priority rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi priority rules among agnatic heirs in inheritance distribution.

Core Idea
Among agnates, proximity to the deceased determines exclusion; extra kinship and precedence break ties.

In Hanafi inheritance law, after fixed shares are paid, the residue goes to agnates (عصبة). But not all agnates inherit equally; a strict hierarchy governs who receives the residue. This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq defines three types of agnates and explains the rules of preference, ensuring that closer relatives exclude more distant ones and that extra kinship ties (e.g., full vs. half) give priority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of agnates
First, differentiate between 'asaba bi-nafsihi (e.g., son, father), 'asaba bi-ghayrihi (e.g., daughter with brother), and 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi (e.g., sister with daughter). These categories determine how females can become agnates.
This is a Hanafi-specific classification; other schools may treat some of these as fixed-share heirs.
2
Understand the first priority rule: proximity
When multiple agnates gather, the one who is closer in lineage to the deceased excludes the more distant. Example: a full sister (as 'asaba ma'a ghayrihi) is closer than a brother's son, so she takes the residue and he gets nothing.
Proximity is determined by the number of generations between the heir and the deceased.
3
Understand the second priority rule: extra kinship
If two agnates are equal in proximity, the one with an extra blood tie (e.g., full brother vs. half brother) is preferred. The full brother shares both parents, so he has 'extra kinship'.
Extra kinship applies among those of the same degree, e.g., sons vs. brothers? Actually, it's among same degree: full vs. half siblings.
4
Understand the third rule: precedence
If one agnate is closer in degree (e.g., a consanguine brother vs. a full brother's son), the closer one (the brother) takes priority even though the other has extra kinship. Precedence overrides extra kinship.
This means proximity is the primary criterion.
5
Apply the distribution among agnates of equal rank
When multiple agnates are equally close and have no extra kinship distinctions (e.g., two paternal cousins of the same degree), they divide the residue per capita (by heads), not per stirpes.
Example: ten sons of one brother and one son of another brother: 11 shares, not 2.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلم تصر عصبة، وأما بنت الابن فإنها تصير عصبة بذكر يوازيها وفي الذخيرة: على كل حال يوازيها وتصير عصبة بذكر أسفل منها إذا لم يصل إليها فرضها، وأما الكلام في العصبة مع غيره فصورتها كما ذكرنا وبيان ذلك من المسائل إذا هلك الرجل وترك بنتاً وأختاً لأب وأم أو لأب وأخاً كذلك فللبنت النصف والباقي بين الأخ والأخت أثلاثاً وقد قدمناه. إذا اجتمعت العصبات وبعضها عصبة بنفسها وبعضها عصبة بغيرها وبعضها عصبة مع غيرها فالترجيح منها بالقرب إلى الميت بيانه : إذا مات وترك بنتاً وأختاً لأب وأم وابن الأخ لأب فنصف المال للبنت والنصف للأخت ولا شيء لابن الأخ لأن الأخت عصبة مع البنت وهي إلى الميت أقرب من ابن الأخ ، وكذلك إذا كان مكان ابن الأخ عم طريقه ما في الناسخ. وإذا استوى ابنان في درجة من العصبات وفي أحدهما قرابة زائدة فهي أولى إلا أن يكون الأخ أقرب إلى الميت مثال القرابة الزائدة أخ لأب وأم وأخ لأب فالأخ الأب وأم أولى ومثال السبق أخر لأب وابن أخ لأب وأم فالأخ أولى لأنه أسبق إلى الميت، وإذا اجتمع عدد من العصبات فالمال بينهم على عدد رؤوسهم لا على الجهات مثاله : عشر ابن أخ وابن آخر فالمال بينهم على أحد عشر سهماً لا على سهمين هذا الذي ذكرناه كله في العصبة من جهة النسب.
So she does not become an agnate. As for the son's daughter, she becomes an agnate with a male counterpart equal to her. And in al-Dhakhira: in any case, he equals her, and she becomes an agnate with a male below her if her prescribed share does not reach her. As for the discussion of the agnate with someone else, its form is as we mentioned, and its explanation from the cases: if a man dies leaving a daughter and a full sister, or a consanguine sister and a brother similarly, then the daughter gets half, and the remainder is between the brother and the sister in thirds, and we have already presented it. When agnates gather, some being agnate by themselves, some by others, and some with others, the preference among them is by proximity to the deceased. Its explanation: if he dies leaving a daughter, a full sister, and a brother's son, then half the wealth is for the daughter and half for the sister, and nothing for the brother's son, because the sister is an agnate with the daughter and is closer to the deceased than the brother's son. Similarly, if the brother's son is replaced by an uncle, its method is in al-Nasikh. If two sons are equal in degree among the agnates and one has extra kinship, then it is preferred, unless the brother is closer to the deceased. Example of extra kinship: a full brother and a consanguine brother; the full brother is preferred. Example of precedence: a consanguine brother and a full brother's son; the brother is preferred because he has precedence to the deceased. When a number of agnates gather, the wealth among them is according to their heads, not according to the directions. Example: ten sons of a brother and another son; the wealth among them is by eleven shares, not by two shares. This is all that we have mentioned regarding agnation from the side of lineage.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq is the beginning of the Book of Faraid. It defines types of agnates and their priority. The author explains that a son's daughter becomes an agnate only with a matching male counterpart (like a paternal cousin). If she does not get her fixed share, she becomes an agnate with a lower male relative. The author then gives examples: when a daughter and a full sister coexist, the daughter takes half, and the sister takes the residue as an agnate with the daughter (عصبة مع غيرها). If there is also a brother's son, the sister excludes him because she is closer. The passage distinguishes between three types of agnates: by themselves (like son, father), by others (like daughter with brother), and with others (like sister with daughter). Preference is first by proximity to the deceased, then by extra kinship ties (as in full vs. half), and then by precedence (closer relation). When multiple agnates of the same degree gather, they divide the residue equally among themselves, not by lines of descent. This is the Hanafi doctrine as transmitted from the founders.

Key Terms
عصبة ('asaba): Agnatic heir who inherits the residue after fixed shares.
عصبة بنفسها ('asaba bi-nafsihi): Agnate linked to deceased without female intermediary (e.g., son, father).
عصبة بغيرها ('asaba bi-ghayrihi): Female agnate who becomes agnate through male counterpart (e.g., daughter with brother).
عصبة مع غيرها ('asaba ma'a ghayrihi): Female agnate who becomes agnate in company of another female (e.g., sister with daughter).
قرابة زائدة (qaraba za'ida): Extra kinship tie, e.g., full brother over half brother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example where a man dies leaving a daughter, a full sister, and a brother's son, what is the distribution?
A) Daughter gets half, sister gets half, brother's son gets nothing.
B) Daughter gets half, sister gets quarter, brother's son gets quarter.
C) All get equal shares.
D) Sister gets everything because she is closer.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, the priority among agnates is first by proximity, then by extra kinship, then by precedence, and those equal in rank divide per capita.
